After completing this book for you, O sons, which is the last science in medicine with its complement, and having reached its end in it, by explanations thereof and its declarations, I found it pleasing to me to complete it for you with this treatise which is a part of the operation, that is, chirurgery with my hand.
For the operation with the hand is laid down in our region and entirely cut off in our time: until perhaps science of it perishes, and its track is cut off: and none of them remained except small descriptions in ancient books, which have changed hands: and an error and doubt occurred to them until their intentions were closed, and the will of its was extended: I found it pleasing to me to revive it with the intention of this treatise in it according to the life of its position, and its declaration, and its abbreviation: and to make it like the forms of the cauteries and other instruments of work: when addition is made from its declaration, and from its operation which is necessary.
However, the cause why this skilled artisan with his hand did not find good in our time is: because medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to exercise before this in knowledge of anatomy, which Galen narrated, until he knows the excitement of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction, and separation, and has knowledge of bones, and nerves, and tendons, and number of them, and their exit, and pulsars, and quiet, and exits of their places:
And for that reason Hippocrates said that the name when it is with the name is much, and when it is with the work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have already spoken of that at the beginning of this book.
For he who is not aware that we are speaking of anatomy, does not understand, and thus falls into the error in which men are killed: just as I have seen many of them, who, being formed by this science, throw it aside without knowledge and without experiment.
What is that, because I have seen a stupid physician cut an abscess of the gross and it happened that some arteries were cut in the neck: therefore the woman's blood flowed until she died, until she became a dead woman in her hands.
And I have seen another physician who presumed to extract the stone that had passed through the urethra in youth, and the stone was large. Therefore he went to him, and extracted it with a small force. And the man died on the third day.
Indeed I had already called to extract it, and I saw from the size of the stone and the weakness of its position that he would die.
And I saw another physician who received a bone from a certain duke of our land for medicinal purposes: and it happened to an black eunuch, who was with him, a fracture near the heel: and the physician, with ignorance of his own, hurried up and tied the fracture with a thumb on the palm with strong strings, and did not release the wound's expiration.
Then he released him according to his desire. Later he released him for some days, and commanded him not to untie the bandage: and he stood thus until the abscess of his leg was cured, and his foot, and then he forced it to death.
I was called to him, and I went to loosen the bandage: and immediately peace came, and he was free from his pains.
However, corruption had already settled in the member: and I could not stop it.
Therefore, let corruption walk around in the member until it perishes.
And I saw another physician who pierced a cancerous carbuncle: and the wound became after days, until the malice of it grew with its lord.
That is, because when there is a pure cancer from the melancholic humor, it does not need to be treated with iron at all, unless it is in a member that can bear it, so that the whole of it may be cut off.
And for this reason, O Son, it is necessary for you to know that the operation when done with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation which is associated with safety, and the operation which is dangerous in many positions.
And I have already stirred up this book in all its places where the operation comes, in which there is fear and trembling.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to guard against this, and let it go: so that fools may not find a way to speak and disgrace themselves.
Therefore, take the measure with anxiety and protection, and your weakness with ease and firmness, and use the better way of grace from God for salvation and praiseworthy success: and let go of difficulties of life-endangering diseases: and take your souls away from him who makes you afraid, so that he may enter into superstition upon your faith and comfort.
For it is more remaining for your glory, and sublime in this world, and finally for your quantities.
Galen has already said in some of his admonitions. You should not heal evil with evil, nor call bad doctors good.
This book has already been divided into three chapters.
First Chapter.
First Chapter. Of cauterization with fire and with sharp medicine, a book divided into sections from the head to the feet, and the forms of the instruments and tools of cauterization, and everything necessary for the operation.
Second Chapter.
Second Chapter. Of sectioning and piercing, phlebotomy and venous bleeding, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows and similar objects: and everything in its proper place, divided into forms of instruments.
Third Chapter.
Third Chapter. Of restoration and dislocation, and treatment of twisting, and similar cases: and everything in its proper place, divided into forms of instruments.
However, before that, it is necessary to say the nature of the wounds and the effects of cauterization of its own, and in which complexion it is shown.
I say that the speech about the nature of the wound caused by cauterization and its effects is a long and subtle one, knowledge, and a hidden secret.
Even a multitude of wise men have spoken in it, and they have disputed in it, and for me, it is enough a little from their words, fearing the prolongation.
I declare that cauterization is effective on all wounds, whether with matter or without matter, except for two wounds: the hot wound without matter and the dry wound without matter.
However, in the hot and dry wound with matter, they have disagreed. Some have said that cauterization is harmful in that case. However, others have said that cauterization is not suitable for the disease which is caused by heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is hotness: and it is unsuitable to heal from a hot and dry disease with heat and dryness.
He who says the opposite has said that a wound is made by cauterization in all hot and dry diseases that occur in the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of man and his humors to the fire, you find the body of man to be cold.
I also say by his words: because I have already found that through experiment this will happen again.
Nevertheless, it does not belong for him to come upon that, unless he has already proven it and been exercised in the chapter of cauterization, and has known the diversity of human wounds, and the nature and disposition of their diseases, and their causes and accidents, and the time of their occurrence.
However, do not fear from other wounds: and especially in cold and damp diseases. For all physicians have become familiar with those: and they have not disagreed in the wound with cauterization in them.
And you know, son, that from the secret of the physician's care, with cauterization and the goodness of fire, and over the medicine burning with cauterization, is that fire is simple, whose action does not harm except to the member which is cauterized: and it does not harm any other connected member unless it harms slightly.
The action of burning surgeons in medicine is indeed detrimental to that which is extended from the limbs: and perhaps it even causes difficulty in the treatment of difficult disease in a member, and perhaps it even kills.
However, fire, due to its own subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless it is excessive.
Indeed, we have not yet learned this from experiment, due to the length of practice and study with the art, and the station on the truth of things: and for that reason I excuse the length of my speech.
And if there were not, because it is not allowed for me to bring this secret and hidden thing about fire to you in this book, and the quality of its operation in bodies, by which it expels diseases that are demonstrated by philosophical speech, which disturbs your minds.
And know you, O sons, that you yourselves disagree in the time when it is most convenient to make a cauterization, and they set a better time for my lesson.
And I say that cauterization is convenient at all times, because the hurt that happens by the time is swallowed up in the wound, which is drawn to the cauterization. And above all, if the cauterization is made for the sake of pains that are necessary and hard, and which do not endure delay: because it is feared that from them a greater malice may happen than the small hurt which is done by being late.
And do not suppose that this thing will not be in your minds, O sons, unless you are vile and stupid physicians, that is to say, that the diseases which are cured by cauterization are not always a return: and they set it down as a consequence, and things are not as they think: because cauterization is not but in the place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and dries up the humors which are causes of the pains, wherefore the pains happen.
Indeed, the cauterization aids the healing process of its own disease, and the strength of its own operation, and the power of its master's dominion: and it is possible that the illness lasts for some time according to the complexion of the weak, and the location of his illness, and the power of his illness: and that it is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in it: and that it is sustained by it in its acquisition from food, and similar ones from their causes, unless an illness occurs in which the cauterization is administered.
A slight illness in a member of few superfluities and moisture, such as the tooth cauterization, for pain, and similar ones, is possible that it does not last in that one pain. But that happens in few.
But my speech is again a matter of delay, that cauterization is the last of medicine: not what they intend in it: for they believe that there is no cure which confirms with the medicine, nor with another after the occasion of the cauterization.
But the matter is contrary to that, and the intention, that cauterization is the last of medicine, is not, unless when we administer modes of cure in some diseases, and they do not confirm those of medicine: then we administer at the end of the case cauterization, and it confirms: then falls out that cauterization is the last of medicines, not according to the intention which the wise and proud physicians understand.
But the ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than with iron, and they did not say it otherwise than for the equality of gold, and the sublimity of its own substance: and they said that it does not make a pus place in the cauterization. Indeed, it is not absolutely true: for I have already proven this, and found that it does not make it in some bodies without others.
And cauterization, when used alone, is beneficial, and better than when iron is used, as they have said. Indeed, when you use fire for cauterization on gold, it does not appear to you when it is heated according to the amount you wish, due to the redness of the gold: and when it approaches the cold, and if you add above it further heat, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls away from that and is replaced by one who does it better and more easily: and therefore we use cauterization with iron here, which is more suitable for the operation.
Indeed, I have already ordered this chapter on cauterization, according to the previous one: and I have ordered them from the head to the feet: so that those who seek it may find what they want from it.
Head 2.
This cauterization is applied to the dominion of moisture and coldness over the head: which are two causes of soda, and the multitude of fluids from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and the multitude of dreams, and pain of the teeth, and pain of the throat: and generally all diseases that happen from coldness, such as paralysis, and soda, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and like these from the diseases.
The method of cauterization is, to treat the patient as follows: so that he may vomit in the first place when the head is uncovered and cleansed with a mild medicine three or four nights, according to the strength of the patient and his age, and habit.
Then he commanded him to make a cut across his own head with a razor. Then place him facing you, so that he places his own hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your thumb on the base of his nose between his eyes. Therefore, if his middle finger bends, mark that spot with a thin line.
Then heat the cauterization of olive oil: whose form is shown here.
Then place it directly on the marked spot with a thin line, using a gradual descent so that you can gently clench your hand around it and roll it. Then gently pull back your hand and look at the spot.
If you see already that the amount of bone in the head is decreased or the amount of flesh, then pull back your hand. And if not, you will pull back your hand with the same iron, or with another that is frozen: until the bones that I told you about are seen.
Then take something from the salt, dissolve it in water, drink it yourself, and place it on the spot, and leave it there for three days.
Then place the buttermilk drunk on top of it over the spot, and leave it there until the scar burns away with fire. Then care for it with the ointment Tetrapharmacons, until it is cured.
They have already said that the more of the finger remains open, the more pus is emitted: therefore it is better and more inflamed.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone: and the cauterization should be held until it becomes somewhat thick with bone.
Then it is cut after that which is hardened from the bone, and then it is cured.
They say that others, it is necessary that when cauterization permeates to the end, until it imprints in the mouth an impression of lead, so that the head falls down, like the form of a chisel: or the instrument that women put infused with the large alphabet: and they consider that they exhale from this place vapors of the head, and the elbow is released for a long time open.
Then it is treated, until it is consolidated.
However, I do not recognize these two kinds of cauterization at all, except in some men according to the fear of man.
And let it be released, with my health it is better with his own.
The head is weakened from the solution of its continuous natural nature: as we have testified in other parts: and especially when the head is weak and feeble, the nature: and indeed the first kind of cauterization is more gentle and better with me, and I use it: therefore operate with it in health.

Head IV.
When the pain and soreness is in a part of the head, or it extends to the eye, and the face becomes wet with the medicine washing the head, and the remainder of the treatment is given as I said in the divisions of the disease, and it does not all fit together: then the cauterization in him is in two ways: either with a hot medicine burning, or with iron.
But when the cauterization is with a hot medicine burning, it is like this: take one tooth, and cut it out, and cut off the ends of its two sides. Then divide the painful place at the time when the phlebotomist makes a wide cut, until there is under the skin a place where the tooth can catch.
Therefore insert it into the same place under the skin until it is hidden: then tighten it above it with a gentle constriction, and let it stay for fifteen hours, then dissolve the tooth, and remove the alien, and leave it for two or three days, or four: then put a submerged belly on it, until the place becomes pussy: then care for it with ointment until it is cured.
If you wish to perform this with some of the medicines that I have mentioned as burning in the twelfth book of my treatise on medicines for the Middle Ages.

It is called the Clauilis: for its form is like that of the scalp, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle there is a small prominence.

And raise your hand, so that the artery beneath is not burned and the flow of blood is not obstructed.

In the method of cauterization in torture.
Chapter VII.
Torture which is practiced with cauterization, is not but from those species which happen from phlegm, according to what we said in the division of diseases.

And then place your cauterization on the opposite side of the weak one. For hardening does not happen, unless in the part which appears to be healthy.
And the form of the cauterization is, that it cauterizes itself with Cauterization in direct contact with the upper extremity of the ear, sub-cornu of the head, quite: and another at a different time: whose length is according to the length of the finger. And this is the form of the cauterization, and it is a species from the knife, whose form was mentioned before: verily it is not too fine, as you see: and it is necessary for it to be a knife with a superfluous bulk quite.
Then attend to the location, with that which precedes: until it is healed.

The method of cauterization in the softening of the eyelids.
When the eyelid is softened by disease or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with a single cauterization, with this cauterization of the moon.
And if you wish, cauterize it above two eyebrows with two cauterizations in all parts: and they will lengthen by two times: and the length of the cauterization should be according to the length of the eyebrows: and do not finally extend your hand with the cauterization, but according to the amount that becomes third eyelid.
The method of cauterizing the eyelid when the eyebrows become prickly and painful.
The cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either with fire, or with a burning medicine.
In the cauterization with fire, order the weak man to go before that, so that he may let go of his hairs, if any of them are covered by them, until they become long and grow again. If however they prick him at his own point: then bind his eyes with a thread, so that they may not move, until they are born.
When they are born and open their eyes, then place the weak head in your side: then make signs on the eyelids of his eyes with a burning iron, according to the figure of the myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the sign be near the hair.
Then place a drunken whey on the white part of the eye: or on the silky mucus over the eye.
Then make a cauterization, whose form is this.
Then cauterize on the figure which you have gradually made in many eyes, until the surface of the skin is completely burned, as the figure of the myrtle leaf appears truly.
And the sign of your healing work is: if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted, and the hair shaved at the point of the eye.
Then shave your hand, and release it three days later.
Then place on it a whey with honey, until the scar is removed. Then care for it with ointment, until it heals.
If any hair remains after the hour, and the eyelid becomes soft: then repeat the cauterization on that place, as you have done at first.
If the hair is at the bottom: then cauterize it itself, until it grows to its natural place: and let it be as if it does not prick the eye.
It is as if you were making the patient weak, so that he may let go of the hair, until they grow and appear. The shape of the myrtle leaf from a paper sheet.
Then take from soap known, and from a shoe not saturated, one pound of weight, or almost that: then grind it all at once with good contrition, and make it with haste, so that it does not fail. Then take from the dough that you made as the shape of the myrtle leaf, and place it directly on the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a dampened wool, in the albumen: and let the weak head be in your groove.
And place your finger over the medicine, and press it slightly. And move it as often as you feel the weak tingling of the medicine, because its tingling is like fire.
While he persisted with this that he found the tingling, then let go of the medicine, and press it with your finger. When the tingling is at rest, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider if you see the eyelid rising, as it rises with the contraction like fire, or with incision, it is well: and if not, then try again over it from the medicine at that place, where the medicine does not press, and does not deny, until your operation is equal, and the eye contracts.
Then place over it the wool with butter, until the fire-scarred skin is removed. Then care for it with ointment of diaphoric unguent, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you at the operation, to keep the last care, lest something from the medicine falls into the eye.
That if the eyelid is softened after a day, and something from the hair clings to the eye, then try the medicine again over that place which you softened with the eyelid properly, as you did at first. Then take care of it itself, until it heals.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And you know that the eyes of humans are diversified in size and proportion. Therefore, according to this, your consideration is: and not hidden is the desire for the rightness of that, which is sought in this art.
¶ About the method of cauterization in the tear duct.
When you are treating the tear duct fistula, when as we said in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not agree with it: then, it is necessary for you to cauterize it according to this method.
Please advise the patient to place his head in your groove, and hold his head with his own hand in this way, so that it does not move, nor does he move with his head.
Then place the infused cork in the eye socket, or in the siliceous ointment on the eye of the patient: then heat the cauterization, whose form is this.
Let it be thick, as the form of a feather of a quill wants, with which the cauterization is made: and if you want it to pass through to the other end, and if you want it to rise thus, try.
Nevertheless, this thickness is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and take out from it healthy matter, and scrape it: and if it is not open, then open it, and take out the pus of it.
Then place on it then the cauterization that is made hot gently.
And hold it with your hand as much as possible near the cauterization between the eye and the nose, so that your hand does not slip, or the weak one is disturbed: and place the cauterization in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If then you are careful at the beginning of Cauterization from the beginning to the mouth, it will be well. And if not: then do Cauterization once, or twice, if you need that: and let that be three days.
Then put on the poultice with honey, and care for it with the dried ointment until it heals.
If however more than forty days have passed and it does not heal: then put on top of it sharp medicine for the corrosive ulcer, until the mouth is exposed: and rase it according to what comes in the chapter of it.
And there is another way of Cauterization fistula, which some at first said. Understand to the place of the fistula, and find it: then put in the same fissure of the skin with a thin needle, that is, a thin cannula whose form is this. And pour in it the quantity of a drachm of lead melted, and hold your hand with a good retention of the needle, and do not tremble at all so that it does not run, or drip the melted lead to the eye of it.
And it is necessary that you put on top of the weak eye a poultice soaked in almond milk or in water.
For the lead burns the place of the fistula, and heals it by a miraculous cure.
If the fistula is healed, with what we said from Cauterization and cure, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to make a nostril opening and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what it wants in its own place.
¶ About the way of Cauterization in the fissures of the Lips.
Many times, fissures in the lip are called "pilus," and especially in the lips of children.
When you treat these fissures, when you consider what we have said about the division of diseases, and the treatment does not heal, then a small cauterization knife, in this shape, should be used.
And its cure should be according to the sharpness of the knife.

¶ Method of cauterization in the mouth fistula.
When an abscess occurs in the root of the gums, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and bursts: afterwards, it becomes suppurated and the pus runs and forms a fistula: then care for it and its treatment does not heal, then it is necessary to use hot cauterization according to the amount that is taken in the fistula. Then insert the hot knife into the fistula opening and hold your hand, until the heated knife reaches the deep part of it and its end: do this once or twice.
Then care for it after that, until it heals according to what we have said about the treatment.
If then the pus is cut off and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the rotten bone according to what does not want to grow in its head.
¶ Method of cauterization in the gums and softened teeth.
When the ginger is softened due to moisture, and the teeth are moved, and it is treated with medicines, and does not fuse: then place the weak head in your side seam.

And scrape your hand: then repeat the cauterization as many times as you wish.
Then fill the weak mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour: and spit it out.
For the tooth is strengthened, and the softened ginger is held together, and the moisture is dried out.
¶ About the method of cauterization in tooth pain.
When the tooth pain is due to coldness, or there is coldness in the tooth itself, or it is frozen, and the treatment does not heal with medicines: then the cauterization is in the tooth itself in two ways: either with honey, or with fire.
However, the cauterization of it with honey is as follows: take honey in a mortar and mix it with vinegar, and heat it in a lead pot, or in a pan. Then take a piece of wax, and apply it to the end of the tooth. Then immerse it in the heated vinegar: and place it quickly on the painful tooth, and hold it for a moment until it strengthens: then repeat it several times until the heat of fire reaches the root of the tooth.
If you wish, immerse a thread or a piece of cloth in cold butter, and place it directly on the tooth that is aching: then place a heated iron on top, until the heat reaches the depth of the tooth's root.
However, when the heat is applied to it, as you would to a copper or iron tube. And there should be some bulkiness in the body of the tooth, so that the heat of the iron does not penetrate the weak bone.
Then apply the cauterization, whose form is to be avoided: and place it directly on the tooth: and hold your hand there, until the cauterization has hardened.
Do this several times, for the pain will be relieved, either on the same day or on another.
And it is necessary for the impression of that cauterization to fill the weak bone of the tooth, and hold it for an hour: then withdraw it.
And this is the form of the cauterization.
Apply the cauterization wherever you wish, according to what is possible: and this is the form of the tube.

Afterwards, release him for three days, and place a cloth soaked in butter over the wound, until the burned part is removed.
Then care for it with toothpaste, until the form of the cannula heals.

And three cauterizations from the back: one in it that is between two spoons: and two cauterizations from the two sides of the chest, lower cauterization that is between two spoons.
It does not become you to hold your hand with the cauteries, rather it should be clear smelling skin.
Some ancient ones have said that out of humans who use cauteries made from similar metal rays: and they burn them, and thrust them inside the belly, until it comes to the apostema, and issues forth with pus, as we say in the apostema of Epagathus.
But in this puncture with the cauteries there is fear, that either a weak one dies immediately, or it happens in the place of the fistula, which is not cured.

Then release the open caustic so that it emits pus for a long time.

The form of the caustic with which the belly is cauterized should be a plug: according to which form precedes it: and its form with which the back is cauterized should be an ointment according to which form precedes it.

¶ Regimen for when it falls into the Aumen.
All that falls into the Aumen is one of four kinds: either a mineral stone, or one like a stone, such as iron and copper: or it is from a plant, such as chestnut and sesame: or it is a flowing substance, such as water, vinegar, and those like it: or some animal.
When then a stone or a kind of stone not added to it grows in the Aumen, expose the Aumen alone: if then you see a stone, then distill something from olive oil or vinegar into the Aumen. If you see the eye already dressed with clean linen, that is good; and if not, then repeat the plaster, the mustard seeds, the tied-up eye, and the waters until it is healed.
¶ About the cutting of the king's linen.
Chapter XXI.
When the linen of the eye is torn, then it should be mended and go out beyond the eyelids like the grain of wheat, and spoil the appearance of man because of this, and it may insert itself: then the operation is done in it as I will tell you: and it is like this: that you thrust an acumen into the root of the linen from the lower part to the upper part.
Then thrust another acumen into it where the thread is doubled from the watery part, and make it pierce: and release the first according to its own position.
Then let the thread be inserted at the place of the doubled one, and tie it with that part of the linen around the acumen: and tie it tightly.
Then extract the eye socket and place a piece of infused linen over it on the alveolus of the eye: and release it, until the thread falls with the king.
Then take care of the eye with it, so that it strengthens it, until the wound heals.
And when the thread is tied around all parts with a circle from linen, until it adds great prominence to the eye.
Then let it be washed with fine sand, which reaches the depth of the eye, and moistens the alveolus, and the eye comes down, and enters immediately: then tie it up, until it heals.
¶ About the cure of Alcomnati.
Chapter 22.
This disease called Alcomnati is not, except for pus, which is gathered in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not itself.
And the mode of operating in it is, as you make the weak sit on a prepared or directed seat.
Then take the head of it with your hands from two parts, and move it, until you see healthy wounds to heal the lower eyes of yours. Then it is shaped and does not go down, and the light is released: and the weak sees as he saw: and if it does not go down below, you know that it is water.
But if it is not prepared for the descent of pus with it, which I said, then make the weak sit between your hands. Then take fine sand, and find with it above the thin lining of the cornea at the end of the conjunctiva with the corneal layer, until the pus comes down.
And when it comes out, then pour hot water into the eye in which you mixed honey: or water in which you have already boiled Greek must and honey: then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
On the treatment of water that has descended into the eye, or cataract.
Chapter 23.
I have already mentioned the types of water in division, and which are suitable for making a hole in the speech, declare and explain them, then take this same according to its health.
Then it is necessary that you make the infirm sit with his feet square between your hands, opposite to the light, near the sun: and tie the sound eye of him, and pull it gently: then pull the eyelid of his eye with your right hand, if the eye from which the water comes is the left: or with your left hand, if the eye is on the right side.
Then take your right hand with a cloth, if the eye is on the left: or with your left hand, if the eye is on the right side.
Then place the edge of the cloth near the corona by the size of the radius in the white eye apparent lachrymal of lesser: then pull the cloth with force: and you will roll your hand with it, until it penetrates into the vitreous humor of the eye: and you will feel that the cloth is already wet to the work.
And it is necessary that the measurement of the cloth be to the depth, the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black part: and it is the corona of the eye. You will see it in the same pupil vision of the eye, because of the clarity of the corneal layer.
Then place the cloth up to the place where the water is. Then press it down with your finger one after another.
If then the water comes down immediately, then the infirm will see this above what it opens its own eye at once, and the cloth in his eye.
Then you will rest for a short time. If then water descends, then place it secondly, excluding that it goes to the dung.
When then it is made and does not rise: then take out the dung with ease: and you turn your hand slightly.
Then dissolve something in water from clear-eyed stone gem: and wash the eye with it when exhausted. Then place all the plaster around the eye, or infused wool with rose oil, and clear eye: and tie the healthy eye to it.
But we, and they who are of our time, place over him ground almond with rose oil.
What if it does not submit to you the dung for entry into the eye because of its hardness, since it is from a man whose eye is hard: then it is necessary that you take Alberid soap, which is called, because of this form.
Therefore, with it, when you are connected to it alone, and not finally with your hand in the hole: and there is no other than to make a light to the subtle dung place.
Then introduce the dung, according to what we have said.
And at the end of the work, prepare an infirm sleeping bed, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark house: and forbid all movements and cries: and place the food of him that lenients its nature: and it will not turn its head to the right or left.
And let the bandage be according to its own arrangement until the third day.
Then dissolve it in that dark house, and try his sight: and make him see that thing. Then reduce the ligament up to the seventh day.
And it should not be done at the time of treatment, or immediately after the incision: rather, it should be left to itself, because water rises quickly through a vigorous aspect.
If, however, an inflammation of the eye occurs: then it is necessary to reduce the eye before the seventh day: and then correct that with what soothes the inflammation until it is sated, then remove the same humor from his mouth, and place over his face which is being treated with that humor for those days which are necessary in that dark house.
Then he should gradually leave the house and be cured in his own cases.
And you know that the student is not excused from sighting a few times in salve: for then he dares to oversee the operation.
And already some of them have come to us who are from Al-Layrach, who said that it was made in Al-Layrach with a perforation, through which water is thought to pass.
Indeed I do not know anyone in your land who made this: nor have I read it in any of the ancient books: and it is possible that it is new.
And these are the forms of species as they stand on them, which one who knows them does not know.
Let them be made of proper air: and their extremities should be with this same fine triangular shape, and an acute angle.
Chapter 24.
§ About the care of the flesh-born in the nose.
When sometimes these flesh-born are born in the nose, there is something in them which resembles the scorpion of many feet: and from this comes cancerous flesh, lard, and white flesh: and from this comes the soft flesh, not white.
In this, therefore, the soft, non-deceptive, and cancer-free part of these flesh, you should have the weak sit down between your hands facing away, open its nostrils, and pull out the hair from these parts: then take them to the outside, and cut what you have grasped with the soft and sharp foam from one side, until you know that the entire flesh has been removed.
If anything remains of that from which removal is not possible: then rub that with one of the soft tools with facility, until nothing remains of it. If, however, blood dominates over you, or a hot blister occurs: then place it opposite as is appropriate: if it is from the bad blisters, then cauterize it immediately, until the blood is removed, and all the flesh is taken away.
Then it should be pushed into the nose after cutting, with vinegar and water, or wine. If, however, the nose opens, and moisture proceeds from it up to the tongue, then you know that it is now healthy.
If, however, the moisture does not penetrate, according to what is appropriate, then you know that there is flesh inside the upper bones of the nose, which does not become wet with the cutting instrument during the incision.
Then it is appropriate to insert a thread of linen, which has some thickening and nodes in it, and place the quantity of the digit on each node, or less: and let the weak one take hold of the extremity of one filament with the thumb, or with what is possible, after making it similar to the one he has made for himself: and draw out the sweet one, until it reaches the caassum, and go up over his throat.
Indeed, many children indeed imitate this dissection in schools: it is an easy matter for him who wishes it.
Then place the two ends of the child's penis, one end that is going over the nose, and the other that remains in the nose. Then and apply a tight bandage of flesh with the knots that are in the child's penis. Do this until you know that the flesh is already with the knots of the child's penis.
Then pull out the thread: and place it in the nose after washing the nostrils with the Egyptian ointment that you have drunk: do this for three days, or more, until the ointment dissolves all that remains of the flesh.
Then place the end of the thing in the nose a lead tube, for some days until it heals.
If however, he needs care that dries out, use that.
To make the head purge, with which olives and other medicines are distilled in the nose, make it of silver or air: which is similar to a small lamp, open like a concha: and its mouth similarly.
And if you want to make a closed tube, like a cane.
And the concha instrument for making the head purge should be full, detected: which has a handle in its end, with which you hold it, when you heat in it oil, or what you want from burning wood, and things that flow.
Caput XXV.
Indeed, a head is born at the end of Thelul's nose, and it grows and increases with the days until a good appearance is made of it.
It is therefore necessary, for that reason, to appear at the beginning of its appearance and remove everything of it. Then place over the place, or cauterant which is burning the medicine that is in its place.
If then the incision of it is slow to grow until it becomes large, then consider it, if it is made of stone, hard, reddish-brown color, few senses: then you do not touch it with iron: because it is a cancerous ulcer.
Indeed you often see that the monstrous ulcer of the hand is caused by it, and it happens from this malice that has been on it.
And if the ulcer is a mild touch, not reddish-brown color, and you see that the incision is possible in the whole of it, then you escape with the weak, and cut it without fear, without trembling: and take care of the place where it extinguishes and constricts, until it heals.
Head 26.
Regarding the suture of the nose, and lips, and ears.
You know that when the solution of the continuity occurs in one of these cartilages, it does not profit much in it operation, unless in some men.
Therefore when something happens to someone from it, you should consider if it is a recent wound with its own blood: and then gather the pain of the wounds with the suture: and then take care of it until it heals.
And if the solution of the continuity of the lips has already been separated, and every part has been made healthy: then it is necessary to remove all parts from its own appearance, until it bleeds. Then gather the two lips with the suture, and tie it, and make a pustule over the blood of the dragon, and powdered olibanum: and put above the pustules a fragment of plaster diafinicon, and some other plaster consolidated: and release it bound for two or three days. Then dissolve it, and mix the medicine again: and let it alone until the threads come out by themselves. Then take care of it with ointment, until it is cured.
However, the method of the suture is to gather the continuous solution, or with a candle, as we have mentioned in the suture of the lungs: or gather the solution with thread, as I will show you to know.
Chapter XXVII.
¶ On the extraction of false teeth.
Indeed, many people have hard and painful spots in the interior of their teeth, caused by small and large plants. And some of them are smaller and larger.
Therefore, it is necessary to open the lip, and pull a thread all around the tooth, and hang it with a needle, and cut it from all sides.
Then fill the place after cutting the thread, until blood comes out.
Then wash with vinegar, and heal the place where there is stitching, until the wounds are cured.
Chapter XXVIII.
¶ On the cutting of the flesh of the gum.
The flesh of the gum is often born, which the ancients call abuluss.
Therefore, it is necessary to hang it with a needle, or hold it with pliers, and cut it at the root of it, and let the healthy blood run, or the blood.
Then place on top of the place where the thread is cut, or other small stitches, and make them dry.
That if the flesh returns to it after the treatment, for it often returns, then cut it again and cauterize it: for it does not return after the cauterization.
Chapter 29.
Regarding the Reason of Teeth with Iron.
When the parts of the teeth are aggregated from within and without, and between the gums are sharp, rough, and sometimes become blackened, and then become smooth and yellowish, until the corruption reaches the gum, and then they become unsightly.
Therefore you should make the patient sit with their hand on your shoulder, and place their head in your lap, and rub their mouth and tooth, in which the bark appears, and something similar to sand, until nothing remains of it, and also do the same for blackness, whiteness, yellowness, and other similar qualities, until they become clean.
If something is removed from them that was at the beginning of the reason, it is good: and if not, then you should repeat the reason on them on the next day, secondly, and thirdly, until finally your desire comes to an end in what you wish.
And you know that the tooth requires different shapes and many figures of razors, according to which it is prepared for your operation: the one is the razor that cuts the tooth from the lower part, the other is the razor that cuts between the teeth, according to other forms.
And these shapes of razors should be ready at hand which you see.
Chapter 30.
Regarding the Extraction of Tooth Pain.
It is necessary to cure the tooth from its pain with all your skill, and then to remove it. For it is not that the tooth supplies itself with a bone when it is removed: for it is a substance that is elevated: until when there is no excuse for the removal of it, then it is necessary when you think to remove it firmly, and to be certain that the painful tooth is removed.
The infirmity deceives the feeble pain, and thinks that it is in the tooth of the Saha and eliminates it: then the pain does not depart until the weak tooth is eliminated.
We have already seen this from the operation of bloodletting.
When the tooth itself is certified as painful to you, then it is necessary to scarify around the tooth with sandarac wood, in which there is some virtue, until the gum loosens from all parts: then move it with your fingers, or with the tips of the thumbs at first gently, until you agitate it.
Then place the large screws well in that place, and the weak head between your knees: which you have held well, so that it does not move: then pull the tooth according to its straightness, so as not to break it.
If it does not go out, then take one of their instruments, and introduce it under it from all parts with ease, and stir its movement, as you have done at first.
If the tooth is perforated or corroded, then it is necessary to fill that hole with a piece of cloth: and tie it with the tip of the fine ends of the threads, so that it does not break in your constriction above it with the thumbscrews.
And it is necessary to be very careful when scarifying around the gum from all parts, much.
And guard your strength, so as not to break it, and there remains a part of it, and the malice that is greater pain for it at first remains above it.
And be careful not to do this that unknowing bloodletters do in their haste and the boldness of their removal, beyond what we have mentioned.
Many times they cause great harm to the bodies of men, whose difficulties are such that they break, and all the roots of them remain, or some of them: or such as extract it with some of the bones of the jaw: as we have testified many times to this.
Then it is covered after its removal with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If blood flows from certain places (for it often happens), then grind some of the zegi and fill that place: and if not, burn it with your zegi.
The forms of the sharp points by which the tooth moves are first long-tailed, short necks, thick, so as not to double when they press upon the tooth: they should be like the thick necks of a hammer, until when you pull them with them, they do not bite into themselves, nor double: short-tailed, and they should be made of iron or of those that are not fit for the ends, and in their ends there should be teeth, some of which go into some, and are held by a proper contraction.
And sometimes they become like the end of the jaw of a bird called the crow, and are strong in contraction.
Chapter XXXI.
§ On the Removal of Teeth and the Extraction of Bones from the Jaw.
When something remains at the removal of the tooth which has broken off, it is necessary to put on the place a poultice with honey once or twice a day until the place becomes soft: then insert into it a needle or a forceps, whose ends are like the end of the jaw of a bird called the crow. The form of this is a forceps.
The ends of these are made like a spoiled thumb: or like an aliskife.
If then you do not submit to the end with these claws, it is necessary to make a cut above the root, and pull out the entire flesh, and insert the small instrument called the Palanca, whose form is this.
The end should be short, but rather large: and it should not be drunk, lest it be broken.
If however the root goes through this, it is good: and if not, it is necessary to apply with these other instruments whose forms are like these.
The form of the first end is a triangle, in which there is some bulkiness.
The form of the second end is a triangle, subtle.
And with other instruments and tools which preceeded in the ratio of teeth.
It may also be applied with this instrument that is similar to a large uncino, whose form is a triangle, twisted, in which there is some bulkiness, so as not to be broken: and it should not be drunk.
And you know that the dental instruments are many: and similarly other instruments are not counted, and a wise craftsman has found by himself the instrument, according to which it operates and cures itself.
For from the diseases are made those to which the ancients did not speak about the instrument, because of the diversity of their kinds.
If however the bone breaks from the jaw, or from other bones of the face, or putrefies: then examine above it in the place where it was with that which is convenient to it from the instruments and claws which I said in the extraction of the root, and apply with your hand, whose form is like this.
Sit in the beginning with a slight increase in size, so that it can be stretched or held together with that bone, and does not fear or wear out, until it exits the bone: and restore the place with suitable medicines for this.
However, if there is a small pus in the bone, then rub it out of its own pus, and care for it until it heals.
Chapter 32.
Regarding the suturing of prominent teeth over others.
When teeth do not grow according to their natural course, a monstrous form is produced: and this is especially true when it happens in women and girls, that is, those who are of marriageable age.
Therefore, you should consider this. For if the tooth is born after another tooth, and is not placed, or its suture is possible, nor its own lipping: then remove it: and if it is connected with another tooth, then cut it off with this instrument, which has this form.
It is similar to a small face, and it is made from iron with sharp points at both ends.
And your cutting should be the one you make in many days, and for the hardness of the teeth, and so that it does not move another tooth.
However, if it is prominent exposed to its own lipping: then lip it with the same lip that has this form.
It should be all of iron, and the head of its small points should be as small as the lip that makes the needles: with which it is lipped over the tooth gradually in many days with ease, so that it does not move the tooth, and falls off: then gently remove it, at the end, rub it with some rasps.
If it is a tooth from which a part breaks off and hurts the tongue: then it should be lipped also, until the roughness of that break is removed and made equal: and it will flatten and not hurt the tongue, nor corrupt the speech.
Chapter 33.
In the description of the teeth with golden sons.
When there is a concussion and agitation of the anterior teeth, either by blows or chance: and an weak person cannot hold them together over the part that is chewed so as not to fall: and they are cared for with stimulating medicines, and the treatment is not avoided: then the wisdom is to tie them with gold wire, because silver becomes dull and rots in days, but gold never changes.
And the thread should be of medium fineness and coarseness according to the amount that is taken between the teeth.
And the shape of the tie is that you take the thread, and insert it twice as long between two healthy teeth: then you should twist with both ends of the wire between the moving teeth, whether one or more, until the swelling with cloth up to the other sound part. Then you should repeat the twisting up to the part from where you began: and hold your hand with fineness and wisdom, until it does not come loose at all, and the tie that you make by pulling up the thread between the roots of the teeth should not fall off.
Then cut off the loose ends of the thread with a knife: and gather them together and turn them with your hand, and hide them between the sound tooth and the moving tooth so that they do not hurt the tongue, and then let it be tied as tight as possible while it remains.
But if it is loosened or falls off, tie them with another thread and let it stand firm for the whole time.
And this is the shape of the teeth, and the figure of the tie of two sound teeth and two moving teeth as you see.
And sometimes it happens that one tooth remains, or two after the accident of the knife and the hammer in their places, and are tied as we have said, and remain: and this is done only by a skilled artisan, wise, and experienced.
When it comes to setting a bone from the ribs: and it is made like the shape of a tooth, and placed in its place, where the tooth is fastened, as I have said: and it remains, and serves for a long time.
Head 34.
When the ligament that occurs under the tongue is either natural, as it is from the time of human birth, or accidental, from the elbow that has already solidified.

Chapter 35.
When an apostema occurs under the tongue which resembles a small ranula, preventing the tongue from performing its natural function: and perhaps it becomes so swollen that it fills the mouth.

The cure of two breasts.
Chapter 36.
When two breasts occur between the throat, that is, glands which resemble linen, which occur in deformity: and they are called two breasts: when you cure them along with what I said earlier in division, and they do not heal, then consider.
If then it is a hard apostema of a red or black color, with few senses: then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is a red color, and the root of it is large: then do not touch it with iron, fearing the flow of blood, even though you let it go, until it is mature. Then you will either pierce it yourself: or it will burst on its own.
If it is white in color, round in shape, and its root is fine: then you must cut it.
If the operation is to be performed on the same spot where the hot pimple has quietly completed its course, or if it is about to diminish: then let the weak one lie down in the sun, and place the head of the patient in your lap: open the mouth of the patient, and take hold of it with your own hands, and press down the tongue of the patient with the instrument which has this form.
Let it be made of silver or air, which is as fine as a dagger.
When you press the tongue with it, and show the pimple to you, and it falls on top of your used one: then take a thread, and tie it in the hollow, and pull it out from outside as much as you can, without taking anything from the cloth with it.
Then cut it with the instrument which has the form that follows. It will resemble a sickle: but the ends of them are blunt, so that the opening of each of them is in the direct acute angle of another: therefore take care that it is made of iron, or that it is dipped in blood.
If this instrument is not present, then cut it with the one which has the following form. It should be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other.
And after you cut the first one, cut the second one in the same way as the first one.
Then after the cutting, gargle the weak one with cold water, or with vinegar and water.
If blood flows from it, gargle with water in which the bullae of the bark are cut, or the leaves of myrtle and such like from stitches, until the blood flow stops: then take care of it until it is healed.
When certain stones are born in the throat, there are two besides the two breasts. Therefore, these should be cut equally according to what I said about the incision of two breasts.
Indeed, I have already treated a woman with a stone that had been born between the two breasts, which she had drawn to the neck, and it was nearly closed: the woman was breathing from the narrow opening, and she had forbidden it food and drink, and she had perished if she had remained alive for one day or for two days.
The stone rose so much that it emitted two branches before they passed through the two openings of the nose.
I therefore hastily fixed the other one in a knot. I then drew it out, and a large portion came out with it.
I then cut it off where I could comprehend it from the opening of the nose.
I then made this to her that came out of the other opening of the nose.
I then opened her mouth and pressed her tongue: I then fixed the knot in it: I then cut out a large portion from it, and it did not come out but only a little blood: The woman's throat was therefore released, and she began to drink water immediately, and then she took from food.
I did not therefore stop cutting it for a long time from that stone: and the stone was in the place I was cutting, until it was too long and with this.
I therefore used my ingenuity and cauterized the stone between the two breasts.
It remained still, and then I walked on from that side, and I do not know what God did with it after me.
Section on making an ulcer incision with a knife.
Chapter 37.
When catarrh descends to the ulcer and makes it longer, then it is called a perpendicular ulcer. And if it is in the lower part, which is thick, round, then it is also called a vesicle.

For if you cut from it more than necessary, you will harm the lip and speech.
Then after the cutting use that which we have said in the incision of two clavicles: and take care of it until it is healed.
But if the weak one is afraid of the cutting, then it is necessary to use your skill in cauterization of it without fear and gentleness.
And the mode of cauterization in it is not, except with sharp water: and it is, as you place the weak head in the socket of your vein. Then press the language of its with the instrument that we say. Then take from the water that I told you in the chapter of cauterization, and wrap it with a non-extinguished iron scalpel, neither thick nor thin, and fill this connection with this instrument's form, which is this one.
The connection of its extreme where the medicine is placed should be like the connection of the cochlea's radii.
And place the instrument with the medicine on the same layer: and let it be weak lying on its side, so that saliva from its mouth is drawn out internally by the medicine, so that nothing of it descends to its throat and harms it.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you from the first of it on the same quantity of the middle hour, until you see it already faded and sated by the medicine's bitterness.
And if you wish to take a pill and place it on the extreme of the radii, and inject the pill with the medicine, and insert the radium with the pill into the cannula below, until the pill adheres above the layer.
Do this many times until you find out what you want from cauterization of the skin. Then let it go: for it itself will wane and fall after three or four days.
What if you need to take the medicine again? Then take it again: and after cauterization, wipe around the skin with the pill taken in honey, and cleanse yourself with what is around it from the medicine: and wet with cold water.
And it is cured externally with an ointment, and swallowed with gargles, until it is healed.
Therefore this species of curing is more salubrious than a long incision and less frightening.
When the wound is cured, even if it is softer than cauterization and incision, it is cured with suffocation, according to this method. Combine calamite, hyssop, origanum, rue, sage, chamomile, and burdock, and all similar herbs. Mix them together, or some of them in a pot, and let them soak in vinegar, and boil: and the pot should be washed with cleanliness, and the hole in the middle of the pot should be for the instrument of the concaium according to this method.
Make of silver or air: and insert the extremity, in which is the ginger, into the weak tooth, until the vapor rises to the wound through the tube, until the wound becomes very much obscured.
Then repeat over the same spot, until it is scorched.
And be careful not to perform this curing at the beginning with aseptics. For plasters are added to aseptics, and it is not proper to do this except at the decline of the aseptics, which are hot.
If this instrument is not present to you, then take vinegar and put the end of the bark in it: so that the weak tooth will not burn: for the bark of the bark prevents the vapor from burning the tooth: and this is good for cure with health.
¶ About the extraction of thorns and bones from the mouth.
Head 38.
The tooth adheres very much to the gum, or a thorn of a fish, or another.
Therefore, it is necessary to remove what is apparent above that falls on the sun, and declare to you what is in the mouth, after you have placed your tongue with the instrument.
When it does not appear to you and is hidden in the throat, it is necessary for you to make a human weakness before the food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps the matter attached by vomiting will be released.
Or the weak one may swallow the sharp end of a nut, or the root of a lettuce, or the tip of a dry bread; or he may take the tip of a dry marine sponge and then swallow it. And tie it up in a thread and then swallow it. When he comes to the place where the spine or the bone is, and it is extracted, then he goes out.
If he does not go out with that which we said: then use the instrument from the second leg according to this shape.
It should be larger than the radius but smaller than a thumb, and at the end of it there should be a notch that he inserts into his throat with ease, and he himself should have his head raised up.
And let him be careful of the touch of his epiglottis so that he does not get a fit of coughing, and pushes with it either the bone or the hand of the physician.
Indeed, when the weak one inserts it, this is better: because of his knowledge of the place where the thing attached is: and he pushes down or pulls up his hand with the instrument upwards, all of it according to the quantity that is prepared for him until it goes out.
¶ About the extraction of Sanguisuga.
¶ Head 39.
When the sanguisuga is treated with that which I said in the division of care with medicines and does not fit, then consider in the weak throat in front of the sun, whether at the sun after he has put his tongue with the instrument that I will tell you.
If then your custom falls upon blood-letting, take it out with a small ivory needle, or with a gentle grasp.
If then it is not possible with these: then take a hollow needle, and insert it into the weak throat near the throat: then insert into the hollow of the heated needle with fire. Do this often: and let the weak one abstain from water all day long.
Then let him take cold water full in his belly, and open his mouth into it: and let him wet his mouth with it, and swallow nothing out of it: and let him drink water an hour after another with his own hand. For blood-letting falls down with the sense of blood.
If then he does not follow what we have told him, then suffume the weak one with incense, or with a gentle grasp with the instrument that I have described for suffocation.
Do this often, for it falls down.
And the method of operation in suffocation is to take a pot wherein are young pearls with fire: and the pot be covered with a covering, in the middle of which is a hole: and the end of the instrument is put into this hole.
Then draw off the suffocation, and let him open his mouth at the end of the hollow, and close his mouth, so that he does not suffocate until you know that the suffocation has made blood fall. For blood-letting falls down immediately.
If then it does not fall, then do suffocation often.
And the weak one will endure thirst, and eat salt, and honey, and will not drink water.
Therefore it is necessary that he go out with this diet.
This is the shape of the instrument used to extract blood from the stomach, when it falls on itself.
It resembles a pair of forceps, as you see: unless it is this curvature that is inserted into the stomach. And the end of it is similar to that of a goose's beak, where there is roughness of the fingers: when it grasps something, it does not let it go at all.
¶ About the opening of the Apostemate, and its sectioning, and care in general.
Head 40.
There are many kinds of Apostemata, of different sizes, according to the rememoration of them, that is, one and one in this book: and they are different in their piercing and sectioning from two ways.
One of them is of the kind of Apostemata in itself, and that which grasps from moisture.
And the second method is because of the places where it happens to the body.
For the Apostemata happening in the head is different from that happening in the anus: and the Apostemata happening in a fleshy place is different from that happening in joints: and each of them has its own judgment from their operation.
And from the Apostemata there are those which it is not fitting that they should be pierced unless after the maturation of the sore in them, and the complement of it: and there are those which it is fitting that they should be pierced while they are raw, and do not mature according to the complement.
So Apostemata which are near the joints.
For when the Apostemata happen near the joint, and it extends itself, until it putrefies which is in its circumference, perhaps the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted: therefore it is a cause nearer to the contraction of that member.
If it is an abscess on the main limb, then it is harmful to either you or the member from which it bursts, or through that member.
If it is near a joint, then the wound is not yet fully healed, and it should not be opened if it is near a joint, otherwise it will decay deeply and extend to the inner parts of the joint, or a fistula will form, or it will not heal at its end.
It is necessary to know the hour of the abscess's opening, according to the complement: it is near the sedation of pain, the recession of fever, and the decrease of rubefaction, and the pulsation of the head abscess: and other signs.
It is necessary to make the same opening on the lower part of the abscess, and more deeply: and the wound should be made in the length of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the hands and feet, and in the places of the fingers, and the tendons, and the nerves, and the arteries, and at last in all equal places where there is no reflex:
In those where there is a reflex, close the wound with the member on which the opening was made.
When the abscess is in fleshy parts, it is better to leave the wound open until its digestion is confirmed, as we have said according to the complement.
For if you open it before that, the course of the wound will be prolonged, and there will be many sore and sore places, and perhaps the lips of it will become hard, and its depth will be increased.
And some abscesses are opened according to the length of the body, at the necessity: or according to the member that is needed.
It is necessary to make incisions in the small labia and in the large ones, making them wide; or to make many sections in the likeness of the size of the labia.
These are from the labia where it is necessary to cut through the skin; and the incision is made when the skin is already like a cloth, and is made at the end where the dead part is, as in the case of many, such as in mumps, and tumors.
And from these there are those that are cut with a three-angled section. And from these there is one, by which the incision is made like the figure of a myrtle leaf.
So the labia.
And from these there are those where a round section and a lunar section are made, and similar ones from the sections.
However, if there is no head like the smooth and superficial labia, it is necessary to make the incision through the superficial or flat one.
And it is necessary when the labia is large and has already collected a lot of healthy tissue, and makes an incision in it, so that not too much pus is drawn out at once: indeed, it should be taken from that part itself. Then fill the labia up to another day. Then take some more pus from it.
Do this frequently according to the degree until it comes out: especially if the person is weak in strength, or a pregnant woman, or a boy who is young, or an old man who is decrepit: for the animal spirit of the animal is resolved from animal to animal when the pus comes out: and perhaps the weak one will die, and you will not know.
Therefore this chapter requires great caution.
After making the incision, you should clean the wound: and consider. If the wound is small and flat, then apply a linen bandage, or an old clout. If the wound is large and there are many incisions, then you should insert linen into all the fissures until they become moist with blood.
If you have split a part of the skin, or cauterized it around: then you should cover it with an old bandage, or as when the cloth is tied, or the hair of linen is wet without moisture: and tie it up until the third day.
Then remove it, and care for it with ointment until it is cured.
If however, blood flows in your operation hour, then apply cold water and vinegar, after which the bandage soaks it up: and place it over the flowing blood site many times.
If however, the blood flow persists, then you should give a treatment, and care, and pills which I will tell you in many places of this our book, and by division.
If however, it is in the winter season, and the wound site is of many nerves: then you should pour pills with wine, and hot oil: and place them over the sites.
If however, it is in the summer season, and the wound sites are fat: then you should place pills soaked in water and oil, or wine and oil, and all of it cold. When the third day comes, as I said, then you should dissolve the wound, and clean it, and give in its care what is suitable for it, until it is cured.
This is what is necessary for the universal understanding of the apostem's care.
According to the semiotics, I have already said about all apostemates, how it is useful for their care in detail.

§ Section on the Strophular muscle in the neck.
Chapter 42.
These wounds often occur in the neck, under the jaw, and in the groin, and sometimes in other parts of the body.
And those that occur above them in the neck are fewer and more severe, and are caused by the violence of the wound. And all the Strophlus is within its own shirt, just as it is in the noses and wounds of the heads, as we have said.
The appearance of these Strophlus is very varied. For they are hard and some are moist, and some are malignant and do not obey the treatment.
In that which you see as having a good disposition in the wound, whose color is manifestly close to the skin color, and moves over all parts of the body, and is not anchored to the neck muscles, nor to the tendons, nor to the artery, nor is deep: it is necessary to cut this superficial section from the upper part to the lower part of the body along line b to line g, and extend the two lips of the skin with the razor, or with many razors, if you need that, as we said in the wounds of the head, and then take it out slowly.
And it is above the caution, so as not to touch the brain, or the nerve.
And let the scalpel be not sharp and cold, so as not to add to your hand with the incision, or disturb the weak, and you cut what is not necessary.
But if you cut a vein, or an artery, or forbid you from the operation, then place in the thigh ground nuts, or some children who cut the blood, and tie the thigh, and let it go, until the sharpness of the wound is dulled, and the thigh becomes soft: or begins to putrefy.
The blood is let then, go to your operation, until you are finished.
Then examine with your finger tip the stitches of the Strophulus to others' wombs: then cut them and cleanse them.

Then fill the old gut with the ointment of Egypt that you have already dipped. Then take care of it yourself.

If however you see that there is excess due to the size of the Strophula, then it is necessary to consider cutting off its root and taking it out, and to apply the suture that I mentioned.

Then apply the hair after the perforation with ointment, and similar to it, so that what remains of corruption may rot until you see the wound already clean: then take care of it with the ointment of grown flesh, until it heals.
Chapter 43.
¶ About the cutting of the Epiglottis from the aposteme inside the throat.
The ancients used to cut this section in the Epiglottis, and I have not found anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their speech.
In cases where there is a tracheal tube (synanchiam), it is necessary to omit the section on the division of the epiglottis: because if a passage is made through that, all the veins and lungs are weakened.
In cases where there is a hot aphthae in the mouth, or throat, or both round lymph nodes, when there is no inflammation in the trachea, it is necessary to use the section on the division of the epiglottis to avoid destruction that occurs from praecociality.
Therefore, when we want to omit the division of the epiglottis, it is necessary to separate the epiglottis under three or four circumferences of the epiglottis, or five, by a small section through the width, in the part that is between the two circles by the quantity, which is the section in the sifac, not in the cartilage: and this is an appropriate place for the section, because it is bare flesh, and the blood is far from it.
If the physician is timid, then it is necessary to extend the skin of the throat with a sharp nail. Then he will examine the skin until it becomes moist towards the trachea: he will let out blood if he sees anything in it.
Then he will seal the sifac that we have mentioned: and it means above the section of the trachea, when it exits from it, with what is broken, and by abscission of the tongue.
And let the groin be open at some time.
When the hour comes that you fear praecociality, gather together two lips of the skin, and take only the same without cartilage.
Then administer the medicines that cause flesh to be born, until it is healed.
Albucasis said. The summary of this part of the discourse is that if the patient has already lost consciousness due to the apostematum, and the surgeon wants to operate on him after his death, he should cut the epiglottis to allow him to breathe from a different place, and thus save him from death. For this reason, they were instructed to leave the abdomen open for three days, until the malady of the patient has subsided, and it seems that the patient has recovered. Then, they were advised to close the wound and take care of it until he recovers.
And that which I saw myself, that one woman received a sword, and sent it with her throat, and it occurred when she entered her lung.
And I was called to care for him, and I found him crying, just as the cry of the dead is.
Therefore, I removed it from the wound, and found blood that had escaped from the small wound. Therefore, I was surprised that it had not closed the wound, nor guided it: and the air was coming out of the wound.
Therefore, I acted promptly, and his own wound, and cared for it until it was healed: and nothing happened to the woman except that she had a cough in her throat: and she returned after a few days to a better arrangement of her own.
Therefore, I say that there is no fear in the cutting of the epiglottis.

This apostemata, called the guttiernal hernia, is a large apostemata according to the color of the body: and it is much more common in women.

Chapter 45.
Regarding the section on the species of nods.
There are many species of nods, and I have already said all the species of these in division: and it is necessary to point out this difference between the nod and the exit: since there is doubt about it.
I say that when the exit is heat, and fever, and violent pains, until the ebullition of the superfluous one subsides, and putrefaction is completed: then the fever and the heat are quieted.
When the nod is not heat, nor fever, nor pain, and it contains them in kistis sifachin, which is their own bag, and is according to the color of the body: and it is a stopper like a chestnut, and it is like a brush, and greater and smaller.
They are of two kinds: either they are fat: or they contain moisture. And the colors of moisture are many, as I said in the division.

Then the last hand of yours according to the size of the probe.
Then take out the Intromissive and look at that which goes into the wound of it.

But if the kistin is broken at the operation and cannot be taken out, often this happens, then take it piece by piece until nothing remains of it.
For if a little remains of it, or much, the Noma returns according to the most.
And if it does not heal you, and there remains little of it: then fill the wound at the end of your cure with some sharp-pointed children's teeth, and tie it up, and put the hot probe over it, and care for it with the rest of the cure, until it is healed.
If then the knot is large, then its two lips, and care with it that it may be incarnated.
If then the opposite evil is a small one, or not small: then immediately, and fill the wound with three layers of threads, and release the tight knot for two days, or three, until the wound has putrefied, and the ebullition of blood has ceased: then return to heal that which remains from the knot.

The shape of the ninth, and they are many species.

Chapter 49.
¶ About the section of an apoplexy that occurs due to the artery and vein.
When the artery is torn and the skin above it consolidates, there often occurs from that point an apoplexy, and likewise the vein, so that there occurs in it an apoplexy and inflammation.
And the signs by which it is known that an apoplexy and inflammation are due to the artery and vein are: for when an apoplexy is due to the artery, it is long, gathered in the deep part of the body: and when you press the apoplexy of your fingers, you seem to hear as if there were a cracking.
And that which is due to the vein is round in the apparent body.
And the section above this apoplexy is an error, and especially that which is under the scales, and in the groins, and at the neck, and in many places of the body: and it is a great wonder. Therefore it is necessary that this care be neglected with iron, and that it also occurs at the extremities, or in the head, it is necessary that it be neglected.

Then press the spot where the two ligaments meet with sodium, until blood that is entirely in it comes out, and the apostematic membrane is dissolved.
Then apply the curing agent that generates pus, until the ligaments fall: then care for it with suitable ointments until it heals.
If it is apostemata due to the section of the vein, then it is necessary for you to hold your hand with which you can hold the apostemata with your skin. Then tie the apostemata with the same good bandage: according to what I told you in the good vein bandage, with two parts from two ends of the thread.

Then cut the apostemata in the middle of it, until when it comes out what is in it: then make an incision for the excess skin and let that which is tied be released from it.
