Head of the Lamb
¶ About the apostemata that happen from the twisting of the nerves.
As it happens with the artery and vein, so it happens with the nerves: that it happens by striking them, or by excessive labor, and similarly: and it happens most in the places of helpers, or the heel, and in every place where the joints are stretched, and it is a serious matter.
It resembles the color of the other parts of the body, and it is in many dispositions without pain: and when it is drawn with strength, it feels in it a weakness similar to that of amazement.
And there is no gathering of amazement in the deep parts of the body, indeed it is on the cheek, and it moves to all parts, and it does not go to the anterior part, neither before, nor after to the posterior part.
What therefore comes from them in the joints, it does not need to be with iron. Perhaps it will happen to contract.
In that however which comes from them in the head or in the face, find the skin with sand. If then it is a small amazement, hold it with thorns and cut it off from the root.
And if it is great, then suspend it with a razor and exfoliate it, then remove it, and gather the wound with a suture, and care for it until it heals.
Head of the Lamb.
¶ About the section of the amazement that happens in the belly.
Occasionally happen to some men multiplied in their bellies and in other parts of their bodies, the warts, which are called Fungali, by similarity with their mushrooms.
Whose root is fine, and their head is thick, and their lips are turned over. It is one of them that is small and one that is magnified in appearance.
Indeed, I have seen a man, and within his belly there were two thymele, which were greater than the others: there was no difference between them, white and small roots, and his lips would change color, and they would become moist. This was always present.
Therefore, I cut it and found in the weight of one almost XVIII and VIII ounces and in the other almost VI ounces. The operation in the incision of these is, as you see now, if the patient is weak, and the color of the thymele is white, moist, and subtle root: then cut it with a flat spatula, and let your cauteries be present in the fire.
For many times blood is expelled at the section of this: therefore, if you do not cut blood, then cauterize it.
If you see a weak and timid man being cut with iron, then take a thread from the plumb, made in an appropriate manner, and string it with it: whose mode I have mentioned, and release it for two days.
Then add to the plumb's closure. You do not stop stringing the plumb, whenever it presses into the thymele, until it is released and falls without effort.

The care of hernias.

If however, it is due to moisture, it is soft, and it does not hide when you press it with your hand, nor does it contract, nor is it added.
If however, it is due to blood, then with these signs, the strangulation appears as black from the limb.
If however, it is due to flesh that has been born, then the strangulation is dark, heavy, hard, and appears according to the quantity of one.
If however, it is due to congestion, then the touch of this part is soft.
And the operation in this case is such that you should consider this now, if the hernia of the navel is due to blood from the artery or vein, or congestion: then it is necessary to forbid its treatment. If he takes it (the child), then make him sit on the seat. Then study on the reduction of the hand, and make the child equal in size according to the natural figure: and order the woman to swallow it, and tell him to wrap himself up until he goes out.
The child's exit over its own neck, with extended hands, and its face is towards the back of its mother's. It is necessary for the midwife to hold onto the child's hand, then gently roll it around, and ease it with facility.
When it is equal, then place on top of its thighs which we mentioned from oil and mucilage.
Then tell him to move slightly. When you will do this, then make him sit on the seat, and tell him to lean towards the right side. Then tell him to wrap himself up: and make him swallow it with coughing.
The child's exit prepared on the side. When it comes down to the mother's opening according to this method with the second one, then cut the second one with your nail, until it dries out from moisture.
If it is hung over the face of the child and its neck, then cut it from the navel: so that it will not hold on, and it will die.
Then push the child inside, until you place it according to what is necessary: and tell the woman to wrap herself up several times: for he will go out by watery excrement.
The exit of the twins, or of many children. You know that twins are born frequently: and sometimes they are born three, and four. However, this is foreign, and does not often happen.
Five there are which are beyond nature and do not exist entirely: and they contain them, however many they may be, as one second: and they are separated by the sifah, distinguishing between them, tied in the umbilicus of each of them.

Head 76.
¶ About the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you are caring for the dead fetus when it does not go out with that which we said in division by medicine, and does not go out, and you hold it by hand, then it is necessary to consider.
If then the woman is healthy vitality, and not with any of the accidents which are feared for her loss: then it is necessary that the woman be laid on the bed, on his back, and let his head be inclined downwards, and his legs be raised up. And the attendant shall hold her from two parts, or lie down at the bed, so that her body is not drawn out during the extraction of the foetus.
Then hydrate the woman's bones with soft oils, such as olive oil and magnesium, and linen seeds.
Then the midwife should anoint her hands with these oils and magnesium, and then insert it into the woman's womb with ease. Then she should look for that place where it forms knots from the fetus, and a convenient place for that.
Therefore consider now if the fetus is prepared to come down from its head: then tie knots in its eyes, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its beard, or in its shoulder, or in the nearby costal regions, and under the hip bones.
However, if the descent is over its feet: then in the chest, and in its ribs in the middle.
And it is necessary that she hold the knot with her right hand: and she should place her thumb on the part between the fingers of the left hand: and she inserts it with her hand with ease, and ties the knot in some of those places that I have mentioned, until it reaches the womb.
Then she should tie another knot on the opposite side, or a third one if needed, so that the contraction is equal and does not move to a part.
Then the extension should be equal and not be an extension only by straightness, but it should move to all parts so that its exit is smooth, as happens with a tooth during its removal.
It is necessary for it to be among those so that it is softened by extension. If a part is drawn from it, then it is necessary for the midwife to apply some fingers with oil and insert them from the side, so that she can rotate with them what is held.
If the part of the fetus is drawn out, then the bands should be turned over to another place that is higher: do this until the whole fetus has passed.
If the hand is drawn out beforehand and it cannot be reduced because of its tightness: then it is necessary for the cloth to be wrapped over it. Then draw it out until it has passed the whole: cut it either in the joint of the finger or in the elbow: and then it is necessary for you to do the same with the other hand, and in two feet.
If however the head of the fetus is large, or it happens to it in the way out, or there is water gathered in its head: then it is necessary for her to insert between the fingers a Spatumile spiny sand, and find the head with it and draw out the water: or to break it with the instrument called Almisdac: which comes with the forms of other instruments in the head that is after this.
Similarly, if the fetus is of a large head nature, then it is necessary for her to cut the amniotic fluid: or to take it out with the midwife's forceps as I have said. Then she should draw out the bone with the forceps.
If the head is drawn out and it tightens at the shoulder: then she should find it until the moisture that is in the chest is spent.
If however she does not admit, nor obeys to the way out: then cut the head in pieces according to what is possible for you.
If the lower part of the throat is affected by an abscess or there is hydrops there, then it is necessary to open it until the moisture runs out of it.
If indeed the fetus is above its feet, then the attraction of its head is easy and the direction of its chin towards the mother's forehead is light.
If it is twisted at the throat or chest, then it is necessary to take it out with the cloth that you have wiped on your hand, and find the throat or chest until the moisture runs out of it.
If the remaining limbs return to the head, then the midwife inserts her left hand. If the mother's forehead is open, then she inserts her hand into the mother's forehead, and looks for the head with it, and takes it out with her fingers up to the mother's forehead, then she inserts a thong or two thongs into it and takes it out with it.
If the mother's forehead is twisted because of a hot abscess that happens to it, then it does not need to labor over it, on the contrary, it needs to give an effusion of watery and greasy things at that time: and apply plaster: and sit in warm and moistening water.
If the fetus is above its own side, then it is possible to equalize it: then it is given what I said in the fetus broth.
If that is not possible, then it is crushed and taken out piece by piece.
And it is necessary to keep nothing from the second inside entirely.
When you have completed your operation, then give what I said in hot abscesses that happen to the mothers.
If blood flow occurs, then let it descend into steam baths and administer the remainder of the treatment.

It happens to him after a long time a furuncle in his belly button, which has swollen, until it is opened, and he begins to emit pus.
I am called to treat him, and I have been treated for a long time: and the wound has not yet healed.

This two additions are inserted into the mouth of the mother, so that it opens with them when you roll over the two vertigo.

Head 78.
Regarding the extraction of the second child.
When the second child is held during delivery, then it is necessary to take the weak ones, so that they can retain their thirst. Then make it hiss with the condiment: and stretch your hand over its mouth, and the nostrils of its own. If then it goes out through this, it is good.
If not: then take the oil, and perforate in the cover of the wound: and put in it opening leaves of the matricaries, such as linen, rosemary, and camomile, and sage, and hazelnut, and linen cord, and centaury: take all these herbs, or some of them, and submerge them with water, and put them over the fire.
Then place a bolus of barley over the flask's cover, and place another end in the matrix's socket: and hold it until it flows to the unity of the matrix.
Then make it hiss, as we have said. The second part will come with ease.
If, however, it remains after this treatment and does not come out: then advise the obstetrician to dip her hand in oil of sweet almonds, or in strong mucilage. Then she should insert into the vagina and search for the second part with it. When she finds it, then take it and extend it slightly.
If, however, it is anchored in the deep socket of the matrix, then she should insert her hand according to what we have said until she finds the second part and pulls it out slightly according to the straight line, so that the matrix does not fall due to the strong attraction: indeed, it should be turned with ease to the right and left side: then add to the degree of attraction. The matrix obeys at this point and is drawn out, and is released from its attachment.
If the socket of the matrix is hunched, as we have mentioned: treat it with sternutation and with the oil of herbs from the flask.
If it does not come out with all that we have mentioned, then be careful not to tire from the extraction in its repeated sessions.
Indeed, it should be tied to the woman's bed when it comes out of the socket. Then apply a plaster to it with the tetrapharmacontremedy ointment. The plaster will decay it in days, and it will dissolve and come out.
When putrid, it is believed that this smell comes from the stomach and head, and harms the weak one. Therefore, suitable suffumigations should be given for this.

Head LXXIX.
Regarding the treatment of unperforated Ani.
Many boys are born, and their Ani are not perforated, which the poor woman has already used with a fine thread. Therefore, the midwife should perforate it with her own thumb: and if not, she should perforate it with a sharp sponge: and let her be careful not to touch it with the lap.
Then place over it a lamb's fat, well-infused in wine and oil. Then care for it with unguents until it is healed.
If you fear that the poor woman is about to give birth, then place a lead tube in the opening for many days, and take it when the boy wants to give birth.
And labor pains of the Ani also occur even from the consolidation of the wounds, or from the stitches. Therefore, it should be followed by the consolidation of that, and then it is cared for with what we said about the treatment and lead.
Chapter 80.
Regarding the treatment of fistulas which occur in the lower part.
Wounds that occur in the lower part are called fistulas, and they can be either superficial or deep, near the anus: they can occur in a single space or multiple spaces.
When that superficial fistula becomes old, it opens up and discharges clear white moisture or thin pus.
Sometimes there are penetrating fistulas from these. Therefore, penetrating fistulas are recognized by the discharge that exits through weak excretion and moisture, and perhaps it comes out from the wombs.
And they are penetrating fistulas when they extend to the uterus and to the virga of the female. And they are penetrating fistulas when they extend to the joint of the thigh and to the node at the end.
From the one by which the penetrating fistula to the anus is known, even if it is not penetrating, is, that you insert your thumb into the anus: and you insert a thin tentacle into the fistula from the air or iron, when there is no tortuosity.
If there is tortuosity in it, then insert a thin tentacle into it from the leg, or a spear from the hair of horses, until you feel the tentacle, or the spear in your thumb.
If you do not feel it completely, and nothing comes out of the opening, neither moisture, nor pus, nor wombs as I said before, then you know that it is not penetrating: therefore, to the care.
And when the fistula is penetrating to the uterus or to the virga of the female, then its significance is the exit of urine from it, and its prohibition from this in order that the place may heal with medicines.
If the wound is deep into the thigh, up to the hip joint or to the hip bone: then the sign of this wound is that it pains as it enters, but there is no twist around the hip bone, and there is always the exit of pus from this part, and it does not seem to benefit from dressing, nor does it consolidate with ointment.
And in all these fistulas there is no care at all: and the care of them is labor and uselessness, from the foolish physicians, under whom they are formed.
In those which are not deep and not old, hope for cure with a bandage: according to what I tell you, and which I have proved, it is that the patient should lie weak between your hands on his back: and raise his thighs above his hips, and his hips should be inclined towards his belly. Then insert a lead or air probe, if there is twist in the fistula, until you know where it pains to enter.
If he however feels it weak around the anus, then it is necessary for you to insert your thumb and indicate with it into the anus.
If then you feel with your thumb that it has entered itself, and not between the finger and the thumb, or between the flesh: then you know certainly that it is deep: therefore you do not labor in it, because it is not its cure, as I have said.
However, they say that it is cured in some men by flesh, and from the medicine which is hoped for, it is that a small cauterization according to the size of the fistula, as before, and the hot one is inserted into the fistula until it pains around the anus. Then do that twice or three times until you know that all those added flesh filtrates, which are similar to the feather of a pen, have become ash.
Then take care of that with honey-soaked linens in butter, until those flesh come out, which have become ash: then take care of it with ointments making flesh and solidifying.
If then it heals, that is good.
And if not, then it does not heal with any other treatment ever.
And if it pushes out, and does not go through until the tip of your finger, which is in the anus, and it is between them and the sponge made from flesh, or sifac: then you will see the fistula that follows on the surface of the skin, then dry the skin at the beginning of the fistula, and you cut with it as you pull out what is in the fistula until it becomes wet where the end of the pull comes out, and the fistula liberates and falls.
Then cleanse those flesh filtrates, which are similar to the feather of a pen, so that nothing remains of them.
However, if blood flows from you and dissolves between you and the operation you do on it, then it is better that what happens, and your diet becomes lighter, to cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine.
For cauterization with fire unites good associations, adds the ash of those flesh, and the abscission of blood, and the drying of moisture.
Then take care of that with honey-soaked linens in butter, or with the trituration of wool, until the place emits pus, and those flesh come out into pus.
Then deal with the wound with hardening ointments, which generate tough flesh: and these are the remedies in which there is cauterization and excoriation.
When they have been restored, then they are already cured: and there is no need for repetition.
However, if the fistula has already become inflamed down to the depth of the anus, and extends beyond the excess of the body: then insert your finger into the anus, and explore with it.
If you then feel a test, and between you and it is a layer of skin, or flesh, and it is near to penetration: then there is no operation in that place, unless according to the confidence and hope.
That is, because it is given in that place one of three modes: either to cauterize it, as I said: or to leave it, until you have reached conglutination, so that it may be possible for you to insert your finger into the wound, and curement from the nearest. And do not proceed much with the cut, so as not to cut the firm thigh of the anus, and it may happen to the weakest exit of excretion without willingness. Then deal with that which we have said about this.
Perhaps it will be cured: or elongate it, and cleanse it after you have removed it as far as the anus, as I said, or when you try, or with another sharp-edged end. Then cleanse those filtered flesh which is in the cut, until you can with excision.
Then dare to restore the wound of the whole with the cut, and the higher opening where it is consolidated: and there will remain an open fistula in the inner part of the anus, and it will be more leu.
And when the fistula suits this mode: and it is, when you insert the test into the fistula: and it is in the side of the anus near to the surface of the body with skin and the margin of the anus: then receive the perforated end which is like a feathered arrow, that is, prepared coria according to this form. You should insert the thread that has been withdrawn from five fingers approximately around it. Then insert the thread gently into the fistula until it becomes united.
If it is passed through the margin or inside, then pull out the thread from that hole: so that you insert your thumb into the anus, and pull out the end of the thread, and tie the two ends together: and string them together and let it be for one day, or two days: and as much as the thread penetrates into the flesh, tie it well, until the flesh between the two ends of the thread falls off and drops down: then care for the wound until it is healed and cured.
If the opening of the fistula is not easily penetrated: then make it penetrate in whatever way you can prepare it for yourself, unless it is very deep. For you do not have the power to do this by your thumb, so as not to harm it.
Then make it as I have said, until it is healed.
The shape of the Spatium Milanese in which the fistula is found, whose edge is sharp and the other part is not sharp, so that it does not penetrate what is not necessary, as you see.
Head 81.
¶ About the suture of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows from their incision: and care for the cuts.
There are hemorrhoids in two ways. Either they are within the anus, similar to wool of carbon or prunes: or they are like grains of salt. And among them there are small and large ones: and blood always runs from them, it is one, and they are many. There are some outside and at the extremities of it.
However, those that are outside the anus, are of a few wetnesses, from which runs the white water, or little blood flow repeatedly: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of it which is inside the anus, is like a weak person who has been beaten: and it is shown until the anus has gone out, and you will see that the flesh is reddish to you. Therefore also suspend them with thongs: or hold them with your own nail. Then cut them near their roots.
But if they are not held by the thongs, because of their wetness and their own softness: then take them with a rough cloth, or with a comb made of wool, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them, and sprinkle on them some hot creams after cutting them, so that they hold their place at the cauterization site. Or cauterize them according to what is written in the chapter of cauterization. Then care for them with the rest of the treatment until they are healed.
If the anus does not yield to the exit, then apply a weak clister on the part where there is a small biting, so that it may leave with it what is in the anus, and it will obey the exit quickly, when it presses itself weakly.
But if they are red and outside the anus, then their case is easy and easy to grasp: and it is as if you could take them with your own nail, or with a thong, and cut them. Then care for them with what I have said, until they are healed.
And whoever loathes the cutting with iron, then it is necessary to apply a suture to them according to this manner. Take a loop of thread and insert it into the abscess. Then extract the thorn from its upper part, and make it pierce with the point of the knife into the root of the other side: and fold over the two ends of the thread, on to the point of the knife, and make them be even; and tie the thorn strongly closed. Then take a knot in the thread, and remove the knife.
Do this with all the thorns, and let out one of them; do not allow it to draw blood from its own side.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose or cinnamon oil on the other side, and place the thread over it; and tell the patient to rest. Let it go until it falls off.
When the thorns fall off, care for them with ointments and the rest of the treatment until they heal.

And if a hot application is applied to the wound, let it be placed on top of the wound with a warm ointment alone, or with wine which has saponification in it.
If however you are cautious about the hot application, then place on top of the wound if it is recent with its own blood, and has not changed the air, the boy whom I will tell you about a little later: and if it has changed the air, then place on top of it some ointment until it recovers.

If however the wound has already been detected from the bone, and hangs down, and there is no retention of it except in a small suspensory: then cut it down. If I find putridity in the skin and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut out the entire putrid part and remove it, and then care for that.
If, however, there is an artery or a vein through which blood flows in these wounds, and it does not heal with medicines, then investigate the artery. If however these wounds are small and simple, then the care of them is easy, light: so that this child supports it over it, because it solidifies it before it changes the air.
§ Method of the Child's Flesh. Recipe: Mix one part of olibanum, and two parts of the unburned blood of a dragon, and three parts of unburned lime, and let it all be mixed well and heated, and fill the elbow with it, and bind it tightly with a good binding, until it adheres well on top of it, and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind it up from above with the child's hair, and let it go, and do not loosen it while it remains, so that it does not slip off. For this medicine will not be removed from it until it is cured.
And when it has made the calx alone, when there is no olibanum with you, and the blood of the dragon, and even makes this operation in many of the great wounds, when it comes to be laid on them and bound, and the wounds are recent with their own blood, which has not changed the air.
If he has already altered this air with some other alteration, especially when it is in the time of childhood, then his intention is not in the position of this child at that time. Therefore, take care of it as we have said, so that you put something digested on top of it: either put something made from dough of barley, made with water and honey, until they emit pus. If indeed it happens with a small bone fracture in the bones, and it is small, then extract it with the help of the Gestalt: and I will already say the treatment for skull fractures in what I will tell you.
¶ About Neck Wounds.
If however a fracture occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between the two, and when it is simple in the head.
If however the nerve of the neck has already been cut, or the artery: then if it is a nerve, there is no ingenuity in it unless it is to give its treatment with an intense stimulant, such as zinc, and mercury, and similar drugs. Because nerves are harmful and they contract them.
And do not put anything cold on the fracture: because the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is above the members: and that which is treated with medicines should be gentle, as limestone with water several times infused with oil, or with rose oil and thyme, when it is dry again with sweet water: and other mineral stones in this way, and wet ointments.
If however the fracture is large, then administer a suture: or cut the lips of it with children's lips. Then he should carefully attend to it until it is cured.
If indeed the wound is deep, or it happens to be in a hollow in the lower part of the wound, where already pus has gathered, then he should make an opening in that more depressed place in the wound.
If indeed the artery in the muscle has been cut, and blood has followed: then separate or dry it, or tie it; or cauterize it if the need arises for that.
If indeed the neck of the throat has been cut, or the whole thing, and the wounds are healed: then gather the edges of the skin with the suture above the throat bone, and do not touch the throat, I mean as even as possible, and return it to its natural shape. Then tighten it accordingly, and release it after a few days. Then he should attend to it with ointments in which there is stipulation and exudation until it is cured.
If indeed the bone has made an impression in the bone, then examine it: then if there are fragments of bones in it, remove all of them, or as much as you can: and what is not prepared, release that, until the wound putrefies, and separate and discharge the exit of its growth.
If indeed the wound is recent, then dress it with the plaster that I have mentioned. If indeed a bone is seen in the wound, and a fistula forms: then attend to it with the one who comes to mind in the chapter of that.
¶ About the wound in the sheets.

If not there is depth, and it is recent with its own blood: then you will not put in it the first hour's baby, nor string it up so that it does not retain blood in the depth of it, and turns back to the heart, and kills the weak one: but put in it in itself attracted ointment, and dissolve it in two days.
If however ointment is not present with you, then put in the opening of the wound a dry bread, so that it sucks out that which goes forth from it by moisture: and make it sleep the feeble one on the elbow, so that it runs that which is gathered in it.

¶ About wounds of the stomach, and the exit of the intestines, and their extraction.
The disruption that happens to the small intestine is great, and medium, and small.
Therefore, when it occurs from a great intestine, or the number of the intestines, it will escape.
Therefore, it is made into insertion of theirs, and their suture is more difficult and more painful.
And a small disruption is also made difficult by another way. Therefore, it should be made easier to reduce them if you do not immediately go to the intromission of their own place: for it swells, opens, and becomes thick: therefore it is difficult to make an introduction of its own.
Therefore, a better disruption is made of the medium disruption: for when it is not difficult to reduce the intestine, as it is difficult to make it slippery in these two kinds.
You know that the suture of wounds is according to four methods.
Two sutures are common to the wound suture and the suture of other wounds of the body: and two other sutures are properly shared by the remaining wounds. However, they are more proper when it is a wound suture: and I will tell you one with the exposure and declaration.
Therefore, I say that when the wound is small, and something comes out of it from the intestine, and it is difficult to reduce it back: then it is for one of the two modes. Either because of the rupture's extent, as we said: Or because there is inflammation in the intestine due to cold air.
When it is so, then it is necessary to heat the part itself, just as you would dip a wet sponge or cloth into warm water alone. Or boil the squill, cyperus, and saffron in water, and pour it into the intestine until the inflammation is resolved.
It makes this wine in which there is stitching: and it is better than water alone in the resolution of inflammation.
When you see the inflammation already resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which the althea has been boiled, or the mullein. For this the entrance of it will be healed when it is small.
If however the return of its rupture after this treatment is delayed, then find in the rupture a small extent, with the instrument by which hemorrhoids are separated.
And the first treatment is better when it is prepared, than the section: and there is no compulsion to cut after necessity and the lack of the instrument.
Let a part of it be one that is rough and sharp, and the other part not sharp, and the end not be subtle but rather be less than the subtility of althea, indeed it should be more obtuse, and that which resembles caida, as you see.
When the swelling enlarges and enters the intestine, then it is necessary for it to be reduced according to its natural form in its own place, if possible, on top of that: for it is better.
When however the rupture is wide in the lower part of the belly: then it is necessary for you to make the weak lie down on its back and place its legs higher than its head. If it is in the upper part of the chest, then place the head of its chest above its lower chest.
Similarly, if there is a rupture in one of the two parts of the chest, then place your intention and consideration always in this, so that the part where the wound is lower is higher than the other part.
And it should be administered in large wounds and in medium-sized wounds.
However, in small wounds, administer it according to what is prepared for you.
Then make it so that it is present between your hands, a faithful servant who will hold the rupture in his hand, and gather its lips. Then pull out from it something that follows the suture after a while, and this is the common method of one suture.
And it is, as if you take a needle or the number of needles according to the amplitude of the wound. Then let go of the quantity of the finger at the ring's end, that is, the doctor: and take one needle and place it in the thread in two extremities of the skin, with two extremities sifing what is under the skin from the interior, until you make it penetrate from another part, and you have already gathered the two extremities of the skin and the two extremities sifing: and there will be four orders.
Then tie with thread twice around the needle several times from two parts at the same time, until the two lips of the wound are gathered together by the method of suturing.
Then let go of the size of the finger as well, and take another needle in them, and then tie it with thread, just as you did with the first needle. You should not cease doing this until you have closed the wound completely with the needle.
The needles should be of medium size between thickness and fineness: for the thin ones wound quickly into the flesh, and the thick ones are difficult to insert into the skin, therefore it is necessary that they be of medium size in both respects.
And it should not be figured out in the two ends of the near skin much: so that the flesh is not wounded quickly, and the wound is not opened before the consolidation of its own, and neither are they elongated even with the suture, so that the wound is not prevented from consolidation.
Then cut the sharp end of the needle, so that it does not hurt the weak one in its sleep: and put them in pieces of cloth from all sides, which hold the sharp end of the needle: and leave them until you know that the wound is completely consolidated.
And this kind of suture with the needle as such is more convenient for small wounds. For one or two needles are enough for their sutures.
However, the second suture is common, where four edges of the skin are gathered together with the two ends of the thread in the same place, with a needle in which the thread is wrapped equally in thickness and fineness.
Then when you have pierced with the needle these four edges, draw back the needle from the side from which you entered it, so that the thread falls from the upper part of the wound: so that the suture be like the suture of a band, and put between all the sutures an amount of thickness less than that of the little finger.
This kind of suture is known to men.
When I have closed this wound on his elbow which was inflicted by the sword and was a greater tear than half a palm: and it came out about two palms from the middle of the intestines, and it was a tear in the middle of the belly.
I then reopened it after twenty-four hours when the intestine had stood outside the elbow.
The elbow was then consolidated in the space that was about fifteen days: and I cared for it and it became well: and it returned many years later, coming back to its former position.
And the doctors judged that it could not be healed.
And it was a miracle, that I did not cure it with ointment. For I was in the place where there was no ointment found, nor anything from medicines. I then laid a old bandage on the elbow twice a day, and made him wash it with honey-water, until it was cured.
I will mention two kinds of sutures according to the story told in the speech.
And it is that you begin with a sharp suture: and you introduce the point from outside to the inner part.
When the point of the needle has entered the skin and gone through the tendon according to the length and breadth of the whole body: let the end of the sifac be on the side where you introduced the point, and make it go out from the inner part to the outer part at the other end.
When you make it go in, then make it go in according to this in the same end: and let the end of the sifac which is on that side be out, and make the point of the needle go in at the other end: and make it go in with the going in of your point in the sifac end which is on that part, until it goes through the whole.
Then proceed and also remove the same side, and take hold of its own edge that is from the side opposite to the one it has penetrated, and extract the splinter from the edge that has been pierced.
Then reduce it to that edge, and take hold of its own end that is on the opposite side, and mirror it with this end: and extract it from the edge that is on its side, and make them all equal in size according to that example.
And the sum of this stitch is that it should be like the stitches of pelt hair, where the hair of the pelts is attached: so that its ends on one side of the skin are equal, and you release them on the other side until it is complete.
Secondly, the stitch of the same kind that he said Gale.
This is the report of his speech that he said, that it should be like the example that some doctors use, in such a way that they gather all parts suitable for comparison by nature, and they put the end of the sifac on its other end, and the end mirach on the end of its other side. And it is done according to what I told you.
It is necessary to make the splinter in the edge nearest to you from the outside, and make it pierce into the inner part of that same spot: and release the two ends of the sifac. Then roll the splinter, and make it pierce from the outside to the inner part in both edges of the sifac, that is, on both sides.
Then roll them both, and make them pierce from the inner part to the outer side in the two edges of the mirach that are on the opposite side.
This is the best method of suture, as it is easier and simpler than common suture, and is the suture that precedes rememoration.
Therefore, this is also the sermon of Galen.

¶ About the cure of Zuchemen, and Fistulas.
You know that every elbow, or apostema when it becomes and grows old, and makes a sore, and does not consolidate, and emits pus always, and does not abscess: then we call it universally in whatever member it be, and we call it Zuchemen.
And a fistula indeed is according to truth, nodated, filtered, hard, white: with which there is no pain, which is the union of the feather bone: and for this reason some call it Risati, that is, the feather.
And it is in some hours moist, which emits pus. And perhaps the moisture is divided in some hours. And sometimes this moisture is much, and is little: and it is thick, and is subtle.
And I have already promised in division, then when I said wound, that every sore which does not heal, and is not born in the flesh of that, is not this except for one cause.
Of which one is, either because of the thinness of blood in the body: or because of its malice: or because there is hard and rough flesh between it and above its lip, preventing the birth of flesh: or because it is full of sord and sordicie: or because the sore is putrid within itself, and the matter which is poured on it is of bad quality: or because the medicine is not helpful in its cure: or because the decaying corpse is in the region, and the pestilence is a kind of this: or through the property of the region, as happens in Caesaraugusta: where difficult digestion of sicknesses occurs, and the healing of the apostema by nature is delayed: or because there is one bone, or the number of bones.
I have already shown you all these causes and signs of the wounds, and the treatments thereof with medicines in division: and it is necessary for me now to show you the treatment of fistulas and abscesses, which are made by the manual operation.
Therefore, you know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body. For example, there are fistulas that open into the great veins and arteries, or nerves, or tendons, or intestines, or bladders, or any part of the costal cartilages: or any part of the vertebrae of the back, or any joint composed of bones: such as the hands and feet: and they open into the proximity of the principal member and its like.
Therefore, according to this method, the treatment of these fistulas is difficult due to their origin from diseases, and they do not receive treatment, and the occupation with them is labor and ignorance.
If it is from a fistula of which the depth does not reach to these locations that I have mentioned, and you hope and trust in its cure, and wish to become acquainted with it, then take a tentam from air or iron, if the fistula turns in the right direction, and examine it with itself.
But if there is tortuosity in the fistula, then investigate it with a thin tentam of lead. For lead, when it becomes mild in its own body, and curves around the tortuosity.
If the fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to understand about it with a tentam. Therefore, clysterize from those openings from the openings of the fistula.
For the humidity with which you clysterize it, runs through other openings, and runs out from them.
Then, carefully investigate according to which mode it is possible for you: so that you know that here is a bone, or a nerve, and that the fistula's connection is long or short: or that the fistula is one with many openings, and stands above all of it, with the full strength of your own: with your questioning, as to the weakness, and with your discovery of pain at the compression with your hand on the place, and similarly from the signs and causes of such wounds.
Then, when you stand above all that station with truth, then go to the care according to confidence: and it is, as you consider then, if the fistula is nearby visible, or in a place far from the incision, or from a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or one of those which I said to you: then cut the fistula according to what I have previously mentioned from my narration, and remove what is in it from filtration and decayed tissues, which is born in the opening of its flesh, or thole, and similarly: and care for it until it heals.
If however the fistula is long and deep, and is according to the straightness: then it is necessary for you to cut it into as deep a place as possible for you. Then cleanse it from all the decayed flesh of it.
Then apply a bandage on the wounds of sharp medicines: and thrust it as far as the connection of the fistula which you have comprehended with iron: do while that, until the sharp medicine cuts through the whole that remains in the connection of the fistula from corruption.
Then restore it with ointments which generate healthy flesh, until it heals.
If however it does not heal by this, then cauterize it according to what we have mentioned.
If then the cause of the fistula is the mouth, and it is certified to you that this is so: then inquire into it and cleanse it according to what I tell you: if nothing prohibits you from anything out of the mind, or nerve, or the principal member, as I have said.
If then it is discovered to you that the mouth has a corruption and is black: then wash it until the entire corruption of it is removed. Then take care of it with that which incarnates it, until it heals.
If then it does not heal and emits pus as before: then you know that you have not succeeded in the complete removal of the corruption.
Therefore wash it over that second time, and make a precise cut of its reasoning, and cleanse it with the last strength of your own.
Then restore it. If then it heals, that is good: and if not, then you know that this corruption is in the deep interior of the body, which you have not followed. Therefore it is not for you in this unless you release nature itself.
If then the small mouth is corrupted and it is possible for you to draw it with fine sutures which are suitable for that.
If then there are many bones, then make a precise cut of their attraction to all of them and do not release anything from them with your own strength.
If then it creates something for you from the moistures and there is no fear of the cut in them or error: then cut those moistures and flesh if they are there, and free the bones.
If then there is not for you a preparation to take the bones from your side: then place on the belly that putsrefies it: and release it until it putsrefies that which is in the circumference of their bones from flesh and moisture.
Guard the wound so it does not scar. And tie off the incision you made in your operation. I recommend placing over it, if you wish, a submerged cork ground with oil; or a submerged cork in Egyptian ointment, or any other white ointment.
When those moistures become putrid, and the bones separate from them, the removal of those parts, and their attrition is to be practiced.
However, if the bone is one large one, such as the thigh bone or the hip bone, and that part of it has become corrupted, then that part is a large piece: in that case, rasp it away reasonably until the blackness and corruption are removed. Then restore the wound.
However, if that which is corrupted in it is a large part, and the corruption has already reached the bone marrow, then it is necessary to suture it, and press it all the way to the place where the corruption becomes exhausted: then care for it until it is healed.
And I tell you, young man, what happens to a boy in his thigh: put this example and aid for your operation.
A boy of about thirty years of age had pain in his thigh, caused by something that moved within his body, that is, from the interior, until the matter reached the thigh, and an abscess was formed; and there was no external cause.
Therefore, at that time, the error of the physicians extended, until the abscess was opened, and many matters were present with it. And then the treatment of his wound was applied, until the thigh became open, and many openings were made in it: all of which emitted pus and moisture from the body.
The multitude of physicians was attentive for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw his hand, and the materials that were flowing from these openings in great quantities: even the entire body of the patient had been washed, and his skin was yellowish.
Therefore, let us insert the probe into one of the openings, and try to reach the mouth.
Then I examined all the openings: and I found them to be able to pass through all parts of the thigh.
Then I proceeded further, and applied myself to one of them, until I detached a part of the bone: and I found it to be corrupted, which was already corroded, and faded, and decayed, and hollowed out, until it had penetrated as far as the marrow.
Then I saw what I had found, and the prepared bone from the corrupted bone.
And I concluded that there was no other corruption in the bone, but this decay, and I sawed it. And I had already removed it.
Then I applied the wound healing with solidified medicines over a long space of time. And it was not solidified.
Then I tried again, and detached a part of the bone above the first one I had detached: and I found further corruption with the bone, and I sawed what I had seen before, even from that same corruption.
Then I attempted to heal it. And it was not healed.
Then I detached it again, and did not stop hitting the particular bone, and trying to heal it: and it was not healed until I hit about a palm of bone, and extracted that with its marrow.
Then I restored it with the remedies, and it was quickly consolidated and cured, and this re-operation and section of it was not necessary for the weakness of the infirm, and the fewness of its endurance, and my fear for it due to death, for it happened to it in all hours from the superfluity of the evacuation syncope.
Therefore it was cured by the cure, and a bone was found in its place, and a good disposition was made in its body, and its strength returned to its proper places, and it was turned back into its own dispositions, and it did not cause any harm to its walking.
However if an prominent bone is in the place of a broken body: then it is necessary to restore it thus: and it is: take a ligament, and tie it at the extremity of the prominent bone: and instruct someone to extend it upwards: and place another ligament made of wool on top of the first one. Then tie it over the flesh which is under the bone: and extend the end of it to the lower part: and you will hold the flesh over the place where you want to bind it, so that it does not hurt the binding of the flesh.
Place a board or a tablet under the bone below it, because when you do this, it is not forbidden that it may seize the corrupted flesh.
And it is necessary that the binding be over the place of the corrupted flesh to a lesser extent, so that there is not unity between the bone corruption and the binding: and it should not appear in its appearance to the senses, and it should attract to the binding of its gut another binding.
If the bone is corrupted and not prominent, then at least a part of it continues with its part: and the corruption is in the middle of it or in its own part: then hold the flesh away from all parts of it completely. Then place the wooden board below.
Then cut the wood from the first part where the decay is, until the second cut is continuous from the other side: and the cut should be according to the length of the decay, as we said.
If the decay is in the joint, cut through the decayed joint and cut the bone where it continues from the other side.
If the decay is in the continuity of two joints, then there is no intelligence except in the cut.
If the decay is in the hand or foot pulp, then it is difficult to do it with a tool. Indeed, you should investigate the decay as it appears to you. And cut it off, and dress it according to whatever possible method you can, and with whatever skill it corrects itself: when it does not make any opposition to the vein or nerve.
And you know that the cutting tools and the saws for this bone are many, according to the position of the bone, and the preparation of them, and their grossness, and their subtlety, and their size, and their wholeness, and their durability, and their rarity. Therefore, it is necessary to prepare all the tools of this operation that are convenient for this operation.

¶ Regarding the cutting of the tip and the closure of the bone.
The ends putrefy, either from an external cause or an internal one.
When you are treating the decay with medicine and it does not improve: and you see the decay spreading to the member, which does not send out anything: then it is necessary to cut into that member until the decay has spread as far as where the member is weakened by death or by a greater defect in the member.
And the sign that happens to it is that the member is weakened, until it is thought that: that fire has consumed it, or that it has putrefied after being blackened: until the putrefaction spreads to the whole of the member, and grips it.
Therefore, when cutting into it, and similarly if the cause of the decay is from the strike of some poisonous creatures, such as scorpions of the sea, and spiders, and wasps, and the like: then it is necessary to do so.
If then the decay or the strike is at the tip of the finger, then cut the finger, and do not leave any space for the decay to spread to the other hand.
And similarly if it happens in the hand, then cut it from the root of the finger, and do not leave any space for the decay to spread to the arm.
And if it spreads to the arm, then cut it at the elbow joint.
If however you observe corruption passing through it, and look at it about the hip: then in that place is the death of the weak. And to administer beyond that, is the quantity of strength.
And similarly, do to the foot, when corruption reaches the finger, then cut it at one of the nodes: and if it reaches the heart of the foot, then cut the entire foot. If however it ascends to the knee, then cut the thigh at the joint of the knee.
That is if corruption has already passed above the knee, then there is no intelligence left except release and leaving the weak to die.
And the manner of cutting the limb, or rather binding it, is to draw the ligament in the lower part which you intend to cut, and draw another ligament above the place. And extend the other ligament downwards: and extend another ligament upwards to the top. And then you separate the flesh which is between the two ligaments, with the sole of your foot, until the whole flesh is exposed. Then it is cut or bound.
And it is necessary to put on bandages from all sides with linen cloth, and do not let the scarlet touch the healthy place: and the weak wound will heal up with a hot apostematic plaster.
If however the flow of blood internally happens while you are working, then cauterize the place slightly: or put on some children's abscessing above it to absorb the blood. Then return to your medicine, until it is complete.
Then bind the wounded limb with a convenient ligament, and take care of it until it heals.
And I tell you that something happens to the man in his foot, this is the same thing that I am telling you.
What is this, because it happens in his foot, with the ash that resembles the combustion of fire: and that corruption first occurs in his thumb, until it begins to affect the entire foot.
Therefore the man arose from himself, after he saw the corruption spreading to his member, which he found from pain and ash: and it spread to the joint, and he was healed.
And after a long time had passed, it happened to him that same corruption in his index finger of his hand.
He came to me, and I attempted to recover that excess with the one I had put on his hand after the purification of his body with medicines: and it was not repercussed, and it began to move to another thumb: until it began to corrupt in his hand.
He called me to apply it to his hand: and I did not do that, hoping for the cure of his excess from the repercussion of that one: and I feared even the death of him at the cutting of his hand. For the man's virtue was above the accident.
After he had despairing of me, he returned to his earth: and came to me from it, because he had been healed, and the corruption spread to his entire hand: and he was healed.
And I did not seek this narrative, unless it be an aid to that which falls from the generation of this disease: and so that it have a signification, and according to which it is spoken.
Regarding the care of Sinus, and the quality of clisterization with medicines.
When a gangrene occurs in some of the fleshy parts, and it prolongs the space of the gangrene until the collection of pus: then it bursts, or perforates, and departs from what is in it, and leaves a watery place as if it were water: and the skin which is over it, like a piece of cloth that has been made fine: and it does not reach the end of his corruption, nor imprints in the mouth, nor in the tendons, nor in the ligaments: he deserves to be called Sinus: and it is not called Fistula: but if the space of its gangrene prolongs until it imprints corruption in something of these parts, then it is called Fistula, or zuken.
The treatment for this is to incise the entire skin in the same direction as it unfolds: and especially when it has been made fine and like a cloth: and I am confident that it will not adhere to its place due to its own corruption.
However, if you hope that the skin will adhere and does not follow the last corruption: and if there is thickness in the skin from flesh: then treat it with Clister as you consider for the Sea.
Then if it is large and the pus that comes out of it has a fetid odor: then treat it with Clister as you receive the Egyptian medicine, which is a mixture of vinegar, oil, and zinc, and are received in equal parts, and are boiled over fire until the medicine turns red: and it comes to a thick consistency like honey.
Then take from it what you need: and dissolve it with water and honey, and Clisterize with the Sea: and tie the opening of it, and release the medicine into it for the amount of two hours.
Then extract it with a smile: and do this for several days until the Sea is cleansed and the odor is removed.
And when it is Clisterized with ashes and water, when the medicine is not present to you: and it is, that when you take the ash of wood or the ash of oak: and throw it over it with water. Then eat it, and Clisterize with it, until you are confident that the Sea has washed it.
If the patient is not able to tolerate the Egyptian medicine, nor the ashes and water: then Clisterize it with water and honey, which has already been mixed with some of the ground zinc. Whenever you wish to dress a wound with pitch and honey, it is proper to mix them together, because of the property of honey to cleanse and to wash: and honey makes wine adhere to the skin, especially when there are superfluities of stinching and drying properties in the wine.
When you do this several times, and I am confident that the decay is already removed: then apply pitch and honey to the wound itself, which he causes to produce flesh in it.
And it is that you take from the plaster, and dissolve it with olive oil, and warm wine: or apply pitch to the wound with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have written about in the treatise on ointments.
If the wound is narrow, in which the cannula of the clister does not fit: then enlarge it with iron, or place in it an intact lock of hair in Egyptian ointment, or in basilic ointment, until it is enlarged.
And similarly if it is also wide, then gather the lips of the wound with the suture: and let out of it the amount that enters the clister without addition.
And similarly if the opening of it from which pus runs is elevated to the upper parts: then dry it in a lower place within itself, so that the pus may run down from it into the lower part: for when the pus is contracted in depth, it prevents the production of flesh in it.
If it is not possible for you to dry the wound below it according to your wish: then try, as if you were preparing the member in preparation for the pus to run down from it according to how it is prepared for you. Try not to hold anything of the pus entirely within it: and take the solidified remedies which are placed above the sign, agreeable to what you wish. Extend it over a layer of linen. The linen should be of such a size that it allows for the entire wound to be covered. Then make an incision with sutures along the direct opening of the sinus, almost up to the sinus opening. Then apply a gentle ointment over the linen, according to the size of the opening: and place it above the position, far from the sinus opening, so that the pus would come out from there: and you will not remove the large linen piece unless after some days one.
However, the one who is above the sinus opening is the one that you remove at all times, so as to come out what is gathered in it from the pus: and so you will know if that which runs out of it is much or little: or digested or undigested.
And when you again consider the place of the sinus of that one, whether the lord of it feels pain there, or not, or if there is pain there, or not, and if there is not an aposteme.
When you extend your treatment in this way, and see what comes out from the sinus opening, then you know that the sinus is stuck, or is approaching stickiness: then you will loosen it in the morning, or on the third day: and when you loosen it, then change the linen piece, and apply the ointment again.
However, if it comes out from the sinus after a long distance, then do not despair of its sticking, because the healing of it is approaching, for there are men who delay the generation of flesh in their wounds, and there are those who act against it.
However, if it comes out from the sinus after many days of indigested pus, then you will know that the sinus does not stick.
If then the adhesion of the sinus is slow and prolonged, and then add to the drying of the physicians, let them be such that they are moist in their substance and dry in their virtue, as ointment dyafinicon, when superfluities of addition are added to it from zegi.
And from the latter part of which it is treated, take ointment dyafinicon and dissolve it with pink oil, and pour it over the old wine equal in substance to it.
Then close it up with this and use it yourself.
And it does a similar action when there is no ointment dyafinicon near you, honey, when you extract it, until it thickens, and you use it. Or take myrrh, frankincense, and olibanum, and bruise them all together, and while it is over the fire, make it smooth on the honey. Then lay a linen cloth over it, and bind it tightly over the sinus: and when you have extracted the honey that has been boiled until it thickens, and made it smooth on the honey, and place the linen cloth over it and bind it tightly.

If the sinus is prolonged and not cured by this treatment: then you know that there is corruption in its depth: or already makes an impression on the bones, or in other hard members, or in the ligaments: then treat it according to the treatment of fistulas as I have previously mentioned.
The treatment of Panaritis and the wearing down of the nail, together with the addition of a cut to the digit and a section.
Panaritis is a blister that is born under the nail of the hand or foot, and perhaps it is born in other digits.
When this affliction is prolonged and neglected, and the blister becomes hot: or it corrupts, and emits pus, until it corrodes the root of the nail: and perhaps it corrupts the whole of it, and perhaps the corruption spreads to the bone, until it has an offensive odor: and the tip of the digit becomes swollen, and its color becomes black.
When you are treating it, when you have done what we said in the section about division, and the treatment does not agree with it: then it is necessary to cut with iron all the remaining excess that remains from the nail. Then cauterize the wound after that. Cauterization is a remedy for ulcers.
If the bone is sound, and the nail is also sound, and the additions of the nail are already compressing the flesh towards the interior, and beginning to prick it, and hurt it: then it is necessary to put on a thin layer of plum under the angle of the nail which pricks the flesh, and press it upwards: and cut it with ease, and place on top of what remains of the flesh from medicines that are burning and corrupting, until the whole of it is removed. Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
If the corruption has already pricked the bone: then it is necessary to cut the bone, and take it out: for it is never healed while the corrupted bone remains in the place.
If you see corrosion and corruption about to enter the finger, then cut it off at one of its nodes, according to what has been remembered about it. Then take care of it itself, until it heals.
However, if there is an erosion or a blow to the nail, and pain arises in it, then it is necessary to first make an incision in the weakest part. Then scrape off the nail with a sharp salt section, from above towards the mouth.
And guard against it being cut into the flesh beneath the nail, for you are causing this by the weakest pain, and it will be a cause for adding tissue to the place.
Then take care of the place with that which soothes the pains.
However, the finger that is added to some human hands may be entirely fleshy: and perhaps there are bones in some of them, and perhaps there is a nail in it: and some of them are born from the root of the joint, or it is a birth of its kind in some nodes of the fingers. Therefore, that which is born in some nodes of the fingers does not move: and that which is born at the joint of the fingers may move.
Therefore, of those which are from them, the cutting is easy for the fleshy ones. That which is, that you cut it off at its own root with a sharp salt on both sides.
However, the care of that which has a birth in the root of the joint is difficult. Therefore, do not make an incision in it.
However, in that which is born at the end of the fingers, then it is necessary to make an incision in its first flesh round up to the bone. Then cut the bone with one of the bones of the same kind that is suitable for this. Then take care of it itself, until it heals.
However, the consolidation that happens to the fingers is often due to the man's nature, that is, born with him, or from the consolidation of the wound, or from combustion of fire, and such things.

Then place a thread or softly infused linen in rose oil: so that they do not quickly consolidate, and separate them: or place a thin platinum sheet between them, until the place consolidates according to what is appropriate.
And similarly if a consolidation happens to some fingers with the palm, then cut that consolidation according to what is prepared and becomes the shape of the member.

Of the extraction of the thigh vein.
This vein is generated in the thighs in hot terrestrial lands, such as Algiers, and in the Arab lands, and in hot, dry lands, few arid lands, that is, in which there is no growth of herbs or trees.
And perhaps it is generated in other parts of the body besides the thighs.
Indeed, its generation is from putrefaction which happens under the skin, just as happens inside the bodies of snakes and ascaris worms, and the worms that are generated between the skin and the flesh.
And the sign of the onset of this vein is that which happens in the thigh inflammation. Then it becomes a wound. Then the vein begins to issue from the place of that wound, as if it were the root of a plant, or an animal.
When therefore you see the extremity of that vein, then it is necessary to suspend a lead weight on the same fragment of lead, whose weight is from one drachm to two drachms and a half, and release the suspended lead from the thigh.
When therefore something issues from that vein towards the outside, suspend it in the lead, and release the lead with the node. If it is prolonged for a long time, then cut out a part of it and bandage the remaining part. And do not cut it deeply before it has completely grown out. For if you cut it, it contracts and goes into the flesh: it causes an abscess, putridity in its place, and a bad wound.
Therefore it is necessary to handle it carefully and remove it gradually until it comes out completely from the end of its own body, and there should be nothing left in the body: and from this very vein, which is in some men five fingerbreadths long and ten, it comes out into certain people. And it has already yielded to me because it expelled a man from twenty fingers.
But if it is cut on your day of medication: then insert the root into its opening, and make a long hole through the body with it, until all that is in it from the matter is expelled: and administer putridity to the place with medicines for a few days. Then take care of the abscess itself by the cure of the abscess.
And this very vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears in the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself: and many openings happen to it, and it comes out from all the openings of the branch.
Therefore take care of it as I said in the division, and with what has been said before.
¶ About the cutting of the worms generated under the skin, and it is called bunion.
This affliction is called in our land the Aegritudo bouina: because it happens often to the bougs, and it is a small worm which is born between the skin and the flesh.
When it moves throughout the whole body, ascending and descending: and is shown to the sense during walking, from one member to another, until it reaches wherever it may tear, and then it goes out.
And its generation is from putrefaction of some humors. So do vermin and snakes, that is, slugs, and worms, in the belly.
And it fears from its malice. For when it itself moves through the body, and ascends to the head, and goes around to the place: then perhaps it opens in it, and goes out, and destroys the eye: and this happens often.
When therefore you wish to cure it, and to take it out, then this is not done except during walking, and by the sense of its own being.
Therefore, it is necessary to tie what is above it, and what is under it with a strong constriction bandage. Then dry over it, and take it out from above.
If it pierces into the flesh, and you do not find it: then place over the place a cauterization with fire, until it dies.
And greater than what you fear, is its corruption, which corrupts the eye, as we said.
If however you see it already ascended to the head near the eye: then tie under it a good tightened brow bandage. Then dry over it, and take it out from above.
And it is necessary that he use a weak cleansing of his body, when the physicians are curing putrefying humors with bad drugs.
And let him beware of food generating putrefaction for himself.
¶ About the cutting on the sickness of Nakir.
This disease is called Nakir in our land: it is a pain that occurs in some parts of the body, and then shifts from one part to another.
And I myself have already seen it, according to what I am telling you. I am called to a weak woman in some cases of labor. And she pushes out her arm, and I see a slight swelling in the new flesh of her arm.
And after an hour has passed, I see one swelling to rise with the flesh, as the embryo rises to the shoulder, ascending to a higher place than it can be: so that it is like silver when it runs from one place to another.
Therefore, the pain departed from that place and fixed itself in the shoulder.
Then I sat for an hour, and she ran to the rest of her body until it became saturated in the arm with something else.
Then she told me that she was rolling over in her whole body, according to what I saw.
Therefore, I was amazed at the swiftness of its shifting from one part to another. And I myself had not seen this disease in that way before. Nevertheless, I have seen many who found the pain to shift from one part to another: and I did not see it with my eyes as I saw it in the woman.
And I do not think it is so, unless it is because the woman was of those who are detected by the dry parts of the body for their wetness: therefore, it appears to the senses that the vapor has shifted.
And it is necessary that they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and in the bodies of the moist, of the hidden vapors.
When you wish to treat it and the patient feels the pain of it: then, if the eye is visible to you, as we said, then draw a line above it, and quickly below it: and dry the area around it, until the entangled vapor escapes: and cauterize the spot.
But if you do not see it with your eyes: then treat it with the movement of the body, and with that which expels the vapors, and causes them to be carinated with rancid pills, and pills of serapine, and such like.
¶ About the Extraction of the Arrow.
Arrows are diversified according to their kinds and the places where they strike from the body.
Their diversity is that: for among them there are some which have large points, and small ones: and sharp-pointed, and rough-pointed. And among them there are some which have three angles. And among them there are some which have a tongue. And among them there are some which have stars.
Those which are according to the parts where they strike, are according to two modes. Or if the parts be from the principal members, as the brain, and heart, and liver, and lungs, and kidneys, and intestines, and uterus, and such like. When then the arrow strikes into one of these parts, and you see signs of death which I will tell you later, it is necessary to make an extraction of that arrow from thence, for death follows it in many ways. And when you do not see those signs of evil, and the arrow is not hidden deep in the member, then take it out, and heal the wound.
When an arrow falls on the brain, and pierces the mouth, and exits through the eye, it is because such a wound causes soda to flow, dizziness, vertigo, redness in the eyes, swelling of the tongue, spasm of the muscles, mixture of intellect, and vomiting of choler. And perhaps blood may flow from the ears, or out of the nostrils. And perhaps speech is cut off, and the voice is destroyed. And white fluid may flow from the wound site. And similar water-like flesh exits from there.
If these signs seem to you, then stop the treatment, and remove the arrow if it does not exit.
The signs of the arrow when it falls on the heart are: that it is near the left breast: and it feels as if it is fixed in hard things, not in soft things. And perhaps the arrow has a similar motion to that of the pulse: and it runs from the elbow black blood. And it follows this cold at the extremities, and cold sweat, and syncope. Therefore, you know that death has descended far from doubt.
And the sign of the arrow when it wounds the lung is the exit of foaming blood from the elbow: and the wound that follows the neck, becomes red, and the weak color changes. And the great breath is expelled high: and it seeks the cold air's attraction.
And if the arrow falls on the vein, which is in the breast: then it is near the costal muscles: and there is a great thirst with painful dullness, with sighing: and all the humeral muscles move.
If an arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps it will then exit through the thigh, carrying with it something undigested from the food.
If an arrow falls into the belly, and sticks in it, something of the kind of dung comes out through the thigh, or a piece of excrement, or a part of the intestine that is already torn. Therefore, there is no hope in the treatment of this, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
If an arrow falls into the bladder and exits with urine, and something comes out from it to the outside, and the pain is greater on the weakest part: then you know that it is fatal.
The remaining parts, such as the face, neck, throat, larynx, trapezius, shoulder blades, hip, leg, and foot, are healed according to several dispositions: when the arrow does not hit an artery or a nerve, and it is not a poisoned arrow.
And I tell you that I have seen the nature of these arrows, so that you understand through this about your treatment.
That is, because an arrow fell into the tear duct of his eye, at the root of his nose. Therefore, I drew it out from the other side, under the fat of his ear: and he was cured, and there was no harm to his eye.
I also drew out another arrow from a Jew, which fell into the fat of his eye below the lower eyelid: and the arrow was already hidden, and I only caught hold of its end with the tip of my finger, when it adhered to the wood of his bow: and it was a large arrow from the bows of the Turks, with soft iron, in which there are no ears.
The Jew is therefore cured, and there is no harmful accident to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from the mouth of a Christian.
And it was an Arabian arrow, and those are its ears. I therefore held it above the same two girdles: and it had already been swallowed by his throat. I was thus diligent with them, until I extracted it: and the Christian is cured.
And I extracted another arrow from a man who had fallen into his belly: and we thought that he would die from it.
After thirty days had passed, and nothing had changed in his circumstances, I held it above the arrow: and I touched it, and extracted it: and he is cured, and there is no harmful accident to him.
And I saw a man who had fallen into his back, and the rib was healed over on it. After seven years, the arrow was extracted from the root of his hip.
And I saw a woman who had fallen into her belly with the arrow, and the rib was healed over on it, and the arrow remained inside of it, and nothing had changed in her circumstances, and the woman did not find any harm from any of her natural operations.
And I saw another man who had fallen into his face with the arrow, and the rib was healed over on it, and it remained, not finding him much pain, and such like many things.
And I extracted an arrow from a man of the King's principals, who had fallen into his middle of his nose, and it had already leaned towards the right side: and the arrow was hidden completely.
I am called to care for him after the arrow wound, up to three days. I then cut the pointed arrow tightly with a knife.
I then questioned it with gentle trials, and did not find it: and he himself found the point and the pain under his own gold on his right side. I then hoped that it was the point of the arrow from the end of the arrow.
I then applied the plaster to the place with the plaster where the virtue attracted and digested, confident among me that it would be the spot where the arrow would be hit, and a sign of the arrow would appear to me so that I could cut on it: but it did not happen in the place meaning that the arrow had reached the spot.
I then applied the plaster to it day after day: and nothing happened, and the wound was consolidated in the meantime: but it remained weak for the extraction of that space of days, until he felt the arrow in his own nose one day. And he told me that.
And he told me that. I then applied sharp medicine to it for many days until it was open: and when I tried to try it, and felt the point of the thin arrow that adhered to the wood.
Then I added to the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine until the point of the arrow was visible to us: and it passed by me within about four months.
Then when the wound was enlarged, and it was possible for me to insert forceps into it, and move it, and it did not obey the exit: I did not stop to refine, and to invent ways with the hands, until I once extracted it on a day with forceps made according to their form, according to which they want the end of the fingers, until I extracted it. Then I will restore the flap.
And indeed, the physician says that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored. Therefore I restore it myself, and the flap is consolidated, and the patient is cured of his weakness in good health, without causing him any harm at all.

However, veins that are punctured in the arms are five in each arm.
One of them is the Cephalic vein, and it is on the side of the forehead: and it is called the vein of the head. And the Black vein. And the Middle vein is composed of the Basilic and Cephalic branches: and it is called the vein of the body. In the groin and foot, there are three veins. One of them is which is beneath the curved part of the thumb, from the side of the nail.
