Regarding the utility of bloodletting and the precautions to be observed in it. The quality and accidents of phlebotomy, and those that occur with its correction, are things you should consider.
Firstly, it is necessary to know that phlebotomy is not administered except in the preservation of health, and with perseverance in it, and caution against the coming of diseases.
And it should be done in one arm of three, which are in the elbow, namely the cephalic, and the black, and the basilican. And it should be done in the beginning of spring after fasting, in the truth, and in summer: and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of repletion appear.
And it should be done on the first day, or on the third day, after the three hours have passed since the previous day.
However, the phlebotomy that is administered in diseases does not have a determined hour: but when convenience and need for it are presented, it can be done at night or day, and in every hour, and in every time.
And it should not be done on children until they are over fourteen years old. Nor should a pregnant woman be bled, unless from the fourth month to the seventh. Nor should old men be bled, who have already passed sixty years.

Nor should a patient be bled on the eve of the full moon, that is, from satiety, nausea: nor a drunkard, nor one who is drunken, until that is removed from them. Nor is one weak with dropsy.

If however, the phlebotomist errs in the first drop of blood, then he will go with the phlebotomy to the higher parts, for it is safe and you do not fear any harm from it when you cause nerves as we have said.
And similarly when the Saphena of the other foot is equal to it.
However, the location of the Sciatic vein as we have said, is at the heel on the side of the leg.
And the treatment of its phlebotomy is, to the pain of Anchaea, when it is due to hot blood.
And the quality of its phlebotomy is such that it enters the weakened bath and becomes firm: and he should tie the crus of his weak leg from the side of Anchaea to the heel above four fingers, with a thin long string: for it does not appear except for that.
When then you see it, then perform the phlebotomy according to your ability, either by suction or by transfusion: and it is better, or to cut it by incision, or to cut it by section. For its location is more profitable, and it itself is hidden in the private parts of many men.
For its location is more profitable, and it itself is hidden in the private parts of many men. If you do not find it, and it does not appear to the senses at all: then perform a phlebotomy on some branch of it, and that is the one that appears in the sole of the foot, and the ear-like one: and be careful of the nerves, and make the blood flow according to the quantity you wish.
Then dissolve the stricture, and place the corium over the site of the phlebitis, and tie the place. For it cures quickly.
¶ About the use of Ventilation and its quality.
Ventiles are made from the corners, and from air, and from earth.
And ventilation indeed happens in two ways. When with scarification, and the extraction of blood: and another is ventilation without scarification.
And this ventilation which is without scarification, is in two ways. Either it is with fire. Or it is without fire.
And the ventilations which are given with scarification and the extraction of blood, are fourteen places of the body. Of which one is Ventosation Alnocrati, and is the last of the head: and Alkehel, and is in the neck: and Ventosations Alhagdahim, and are two layers of the collar from two parts at once: and Ventosations of the mentum, and is under the mandible in the lower jaw: and Ventosations of two spatulas: and Ventosations of Alachosos on the end of the tail: and Ventosations of two focils, and are in the middle of two brachii: and Ventosations of two cuffs: and Ventosations of two cuanillae.
And Ventosation indeed does not draw blood from you of the finest particles scattered in the flesh, and for that reason it does not fail strength from them, just as is the case with its effect from phlebotomy. It is not necessary to administer ventosation either with fire, or without fire, in certain diseases that arise from repletion, until the whole body is evacuated.
If the necessity for ventosation is provoked by the disease, or from custom, we administer it at all times at the beginning of the month, at its end, and in the middle of it, and whenever the time may be.
That is, because of men who when the blood increases in it, until they require an extraction from it by ventosation, find in their head a grauedinem, and a sodahan.
And from them are those who find repletion and redness in their face, head, and neck. And from them are those who find pruritus in their face, and on their forehead, and a darkness, and a dullness in their eyes.
And from them are those who experience pain in the place of their own ventosation. And from them are those whose laughter is multiplied. And from them are those who find a taste of blood in their mouth: or they spue out blood, and expel it. And from them are those whose sleep is multiplied. And from them are those who see in their sleep blood, and redness, and wounds, and similar things to these.
When therefore we see something of these, and especially if it is in the middle of the third month: we advise that ventosation be made to be performed, after the two hours have passed, or three.
The neck of the windpipe, is because it carries the old age to the head, and that which is poured out to the eyes. It should be, that this should be after the evacuation of the whole body.
And indeed, this is in the place of the cephalic phlebotomy.
And it should not be used by one who has a cold complexion, or in which there is a catarrh. For it does not bring large harm to him.
And therefore, it should not be used by the old, and in whose head there are cold diseases.
But if he is persistent on it, a forgetfulness is generated for him.
And therefore, it should be that you precede the windpipe surgeon, so that he lowers his hand when it is almost wet to the lower parts, fearing the generation of forgetfulness.
Ventosation or Alkehel is in the place of the cephalic phlebotomy and the basilic phlebotomy, and for that reason it brings asmati, constriction, anhelitus, instrumental fissure anhelitus, tussis, and repletion.
And it should be that Alkehel ventosation is pressed upwards, because if it is laid down lower, it generates weakness in the heart and stomach.
Alhagdahim ventosation brings painful accidents in the head, obtalmia, hemiglossal, perforations, and pain in the roots of the teeth: and it is in the place of the basilic phlebotomy.
And it should be that you precede the windpipe surgeon, so that he does not lower his hand when shaving: so as not to rupture the artery, and to cause the flow of blood.
Ventilation under the chin, wine is poured into the mouth, and corruption of the tongue, and similar to these from diseases that are in the mouth: and it is in place of phlebotomy, which are in two lips.
Ventilation of the spatula, it is poured on the wine, which is made by reflection, and heat.
Ventilation of the interior parts of the two spatulas, it is poured on the three veins of the thighs, basilic, and fuscus, and cephalic: for it draws blood from all these small veins that are in the flesh: and these small veins are drawn from other large veins until the attraction becomes attached to the three veins.
And it is necessary that you be the first to ventilate, so that the process does not proceed too much in the scarification: for the place is bare of flesh, and under it are nerves and arteries.
Ventilation however that becomes saturated on the wine, pours over the anus, and over the lower ulcers.
And it is necessary that you be the first to ventilate so that it is large and comes from the air: for the place needs strong suction, and perhaps the small vents are broken, and the scarification is large.
Ventilation however reduces the bed diminutively: for it draws blood from the whole body, and conveys old pains to the renals, and matriculas, and uesica: it provokes menstruation, and conveys bothor and ademenul: and stand in the place of phlebotomy of two saphenous veins, and alhorcobeni.
Indeed they weaken the body greatly, and cause syncope in many men.
The proximity of the winds of Ventus is similar to the proximity of the winds of two cups.
The quality of the position of the winds of Ventus is, that you place a wet vapor first, and then a gentle suction: and do not prolong the position of the winds, but place them lightly, and remove them lightly, so that the humors may come to the place in equal measure: and do not cease to repeat this until you see the place already reddened and inflamed, and the redness of the blood appears: then shave it, and repeat the suction gradually. Then consider in the disposition of the bodies.
For whoever is of soft flesh and rare bones, it is necessary that you shave it only once, not more: so as not to ulcerate the place.
And advise the Ventosator to enlarge the shaving, and make it deep, and temper the suction in ease, and lightness, and motion of its own.
If there is a thickness in the blood, then it is necessary that you shave it twice. In water indeed the first opening is made for the subtilization of the blood and its aqueousness: and in the second, the pursuit of the sharp extraction of the thick blood.
If indeed the blood is fecal and valley, then let the shaving of water be the third: so as to get the last.
And at last, when we want to draw the blood slightly, or rather, almost, a single shaving is enough for us. If indeed we want the extraction of the blood to be many, we shave it by multiple shavings.
And if we measure that the blood is thick, then it is necessary that it be shaved by deep shaving: and the terminal equal in the shaving, is the depth of the skin.
What is that which must be administered from oils at the position of the Winds, and what must be avoided in inhaling.
In the one where the skin is rough, hard, dark, and the pores of whose skin are narrow, it must be made to anoint the winds with oils that are open, soft, and dissolved, such as the oil of alkali, or the ointment of violets, or the ointment of the seeds of sweet almonds, or the ointment of the cucumber seed.
And if it is in the winter season, then the oil of narcissus, or the oil of lilies, or the oil of camomile, or saffron, and similar oils.
If there is superfluousness that is rough and cold, then the oil should be amaracin, or the oil of balsam, or the white oil, or the oil of anetum: and similar oils.
If inhaling is necessary through large pores of soft flesh, it must be prohibited from oil, and it must be made to wash the winds of those places with water that is rosy, or cold, or cold, or water of cucumbers, or water of celery: and similar oils.
He whose blood is of many moistures, washes the winds with vinegar, or with water of myrtle, and sumach: and similar oils.
Whose superfluities are rough, he washes his own winds with old wine, or with cold water, or with the decoction of anetum, or with camomile: and similar oils.
And it must be avoided that in the bath or in the bathroom, but it is necessary that after leaving the bath, either for an hour, or for two hours, it is administered.
It is not necessary for someone to sleep after ventilation.
What is to be done in order to ventilate, or before phlebotomy?
And then it is necessary, if the ventilation or phlebotomy is choleric, and there is sharpness and inflammation above the blood of the patient: then it is necessary that he receive cold, such as pomegranate rind: and also endive with vinegar and lettuce, and dry iubeba, and similar things.
And then place the meat of his chicks, and lean meats, and cooked foods with coarse flour: and similar things.
And if the complexion is cold, he should take in a pot of syrup made from honey or almonds, or ulecaniabin made from sesame seeds: and he should take a slightly scented wine, which is between old and new: and he should be advised to use it in small amounts. And then place the meat of his chicks, and cooked foods with hops: and pigeons, that is, young doves: and the young of columbaissadebat.
And it is necessary that the drink of the day and ventilation and phlebotomy be more than the food: and it is necessary that a drink be given in a pot in which some men in Tyrian alfaroch or muscat wine, or alesethe before ventilation: and before phlebotomy, or after: so that the principal limbs are strengthened, and the blood becomes thin. It is not necessary for them to take it in a hot drink.
About ventilation without scarification. However, ventilation without scarification are those that are placed on the back, and spleen, and podagram, and above the ventrum, umbilicus, and the region of the liver, and the navel: for these parts do not bear scarification over them.
It is not sought through these, unless there is attachment from a blood vessel to a limb, as we place the vent on the breasts in the case of a bloody discharge from the nose. And we employ them to dissolve the cold moisture injected into a member from another member: as we place the vapor over the ventricle and the navel. Indeed, it dries the member and heats it up, and relieves the pain because it dissolves that cold moisture.
It is also placed over the kidneys when there is poverty or a stone in them. Indeed, the strength of its attachment may open up poverty, or it may remove the stone from its place.
And it also does so when placed over the spleen, and the liver to be heated up at the same time in both of them.
And these vapors are given with the cut only. And they are sometimes given with fire.
And they are sometimes given with full hot water in the cases of pleurisy: and this is, that the vapor is filled with hot water, or with water in which the herbs that agree with it have been decocted.
The form of the vapor given with fire.
The size of its opening should be two fingers wide, according to the form we have made: and its quantity should be half a palm deep in the hollow: and there should be a small hole in the side, in the place which is about the middle of it, according to the amount that enters the needle: it should be made of air at the same time, or of brass, with golden edges, equal to the size of the hole: so as not to hurt the member in its position over it: and there should be a hole in the middle of it, through which the candle is passed when it is lit with fire.
This already has been made soft and wet, greater than what we have mentioned, and lesser than that, according to the severity of its ailment and age of the one who uses it.
Winds are different for children, and those that lessen pain, than those that are for men and large bodies.
The quality of applying this wet with fire to the body is, as if you were setting a linen comb with fire from linen, or a small candle from a wick: and place it on the middle of a woman who has passed through menstruation, which is in the lower part of the wet: so that the fire may be set to the lower part of the wet, so that it does not burn the weak body.
Then it is placed on the body: and a finger is placed over the hole which I said, until when we hold the wet: while we require, we remove the finger, and the vapour comes out above that hole, and the wet is immediately dissolved.
Then set fire to the linen according to its kind, and then if you need that,
In the wet which is administered in inflammation of pleurisy with water, there is no woman who has passed through menstruation, nor hole: and it is not given unless it is filled with water, and is placed only on the body.
And this is its form.
And this wet, the more it is great, so that it can hold much water, the better it is.
¶ About the suspension of Sanguisugarum.
Sanguisugae are not given in many, except in which there is no position for the wet, because of their smallness, such as the lip, and gum, and those like them. Or in a member stripped of flesh, such as the finger, and nose, and those like them.
The quality of these instruments is such that they are made from blood-letting plants that are found in sweet waters, free from putrefaction.
Then they are allowed to remain in sweet water for a day and night until they become hungry, and nothing remains in their bellies. Then the body will be emptied at first with bloodletting, and with vomiting. Then cleanse the weak member until it turns red. Afterward, they will be placed on top of it.
When they are filled, and fall down, and there is a possibility of drawing out the water from the place with vinegar, then it is the last in the operation: and if not, then cleanse the place with vinegar. Then when much water comes out, and it frizzes, and is expressed.
If the course of blood is prolonged after the blood-letting, and it is still residing, then pour linen flax into cold water, and place it on top, until the abscess is separated.
If the blood is multiplied, then poultice it with ground barley or galls, and similar substances from stinx: until the blood is separated.
Or they may be placed on top of the place in halves of flax seeds: and they are allowed to remain until the flax sticks to the place, because the blood is separated.
And it is necessary if a blood-letting is required again, when it is possible, to change them.
But if they are forbidden from being hung up, then cleanse the place with the recent blood. Or hang up a sponge in the places until something comes out of the blood. Then they are placed on top, because when they feel something from the blood, they stick immediately.
When you wish for them to fall, apply something ground or salted or ashed over them, and they will fall immediately.
This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of broken bones and accidents of the bones.
Know, O sons of mine, that you are stupid doctors and fools who do not understand this chapter of the ancient book, nor have read from it.
And for this reason, this method is isolated from our earthly sciences. And I have never seen any good in this, and I have not obtained it from this, unless I have obtained it only through the long reading of ancient books and a desire for their understanding, until I extracted the science of this from them.
Then I applied the experiment and study of the length of my life.
And I have described to you all the science of this chapter: and then my experiment surpassed what was contained in that knowledge: and after I had freed it from the occupation of elongation, and from the end of abbreviation, and from the end of declination, and I showed the end of declination: and I formed many forms in it from the shapes of the instruments given in it, when it is from the addition of declination, as I did in the two preceding chapters.
Chapter II.
It is necessary that we say in the preface of this chapter, that it contains the highest sermons, and the headings, to which the understanding of the artificer is directed first, namely, whether you or those who are quick, know or learn this noble art, and others from you.
I say that when it happens to anyone a fracture, or dislocation, or torsion, or case: then it is necessary that we immediately attend to the sanguination and the dissolution of it, and also of the latter: if nothing prevents it, as weakness of vigor: or it is he who has something from them, a child, or an old man decayed: or it is time of excessive heat, or excessive cold.
Then he should be content with his food, cold vegetables, and flesh of animals, and seeds: and forbid wine, and fat meat, and repel from the food and all food that fills the veins with blood. Then when you are secure from the heat of the aposteme, and do not fear the effusion of the material to the member: then the weak one returns to the regimen of the first with whom it was customary for his habit.
When the broken bone begins to be restored, then it is necessary that the weak one be fed with nutritious food, much and coarse, in which there is weakness: such as food made from boiled flour with water, and rice, and barley, and feet, and intestines of vinegar, and egg, and fresh fish, and wine, and such like. When this regimen is made for the coagulation of the fracture more quickly and better.
When broken bones are in the eyes of those who are in the first stage of old age and decay, it is not possible for them to continue and to heal according to their nature, due to the dryness of their limbs: and they consolidate and continue those which come from them in the end, as the bones of young boys.
Nevertheless, nature connects something similar to glue on the broken bone from all sides, where there is thickening, which holds and strengthens it until they are glued together, and they bind themselves together until the end of strength and firmness, as was in the beginning, until it does not prevent anything from its operations: and for this reason it is necessary to give weak foods, in which there is thickness, viscosity, and thickening, as we have said.
You know that the appearance of fractures is diverse, according to the diversity of the limbs: for the fracture of the thigh is different from the fracture of the bone of the head: and the fracture of the bone of the breast is different from the fracture of the bone of the back: and all other parts of the body are also diverse in their nature: and I come with remembrance of all kinds of fractures, each one distinct from the other. And the appearance of the fracture of bones is also diverse within itself.
For it happens that the fracture of this arc is made, except for the stars that happen to it. And sometimes it happens that the fracture of this arc is made according to the length of the bone: and these fractures are called saturation points, that is, stars, and the additions that follow, as they do in a quill when the pen is used for writing. And not proceeding: and is a fracture with the ulna and disruption at the head: and is a fracture of the small fissure.
And of all kinds is genius, or the proper instrument for its restoration, according to which rememberance of it is to be recollected, distinct in its places.
And from that by which the fracture of bones is known, is the tortuosity of it, and its eminence: and its appearance to the senses, and its sound when you comprise it with your hand.
When therefore there is not apparent tortuosity in the place, nor sound when you touch the bone with your hand when you move it, nor great weakness of a large pain: then there is not fracture there, but it is possible that there is tortuosity or a small fissure: therefore it is not necessary to move it with your hand and completely with compression, much less to put above it from medicines, which comes to memory, after the moment that conuenit loco: then it is drawn tight by a subtle string.
And you know that the place when it is arched, and is divided into two, besides what happens to satiety, yet all parts are removed from their comparison: then it is necessary for you to begin from your hour to the rectification of it, equaling it before it happens to him a hot apostema.
If however a hot apostema happens to it, then let it be given days, until the apostema rests. Then equal it according to whatever mode can be from lenity and ingenuity.
And you know that the restoration of it, and its equalization, is easier than bones, in which satiety happens.
Then draw it tight according to what comes to memory to you.
If indeed the bones are affected by caries, then it is necessary to extend this member, broken into two parts, either the hand or foot: or if your hand, then if the member is small: or if with two thongs, or with a rope and your hand.
And your position when you place the member on a corresponding place according to its natural figure, until the parts of the broken member are extended: then try to make those additions with all ingenuity, and according to whatever method you can in those places: and be careful not to cause any pain or injury to the weak part by your operation, nor any wound: and try to apply one of the two bones alongside its companion bone, according to the better forms.
It is necessary at that time to test and touch it with your own hand. If then you see something different here, correct it yourself, and make it equal according to the quantity of your strength.
And be careful of a violent extension, and a strong compression, as some foolish men do. For they often make their own hot aphorism or contraction in the member through that operation, as we have already seen this from their operations.
Then annex after the equation, and a fitting operation, and a strictly closed member, and quietness, and tranquility: and warn the weak about it. And make it hesitate, lest it move in the hour of its vigilance, and in its dreams at its revolution, and its agitation, and at its evacuation, and all its movements with the last strength of itself. And so that it may not be in the position of the member with the position that follows pain. That is, because when it feels pain or injury in the position of the member's disposition, then it should change it to another position from that with which it does not feel pain.
When setting that bone, make its position equal and straight, so as not to cause twisting in the member when it is restored.
And the quality of the fracture of the member is according to what I say.
You know that fractured members are diversified according to their soundness, and their magnitude, and their form.
Those which are small like the arm, the finger, and the toe, and such like, then it is fitting that a soft and fine cloth bandage be used. But if they are large, such as the thigh and the leg, it is fitting that there be a wide bandage in them, hard.
For a wide bandage connects the large member, and tightens it from all sides equal, so that it does not enter the mark.
Then after your purge, begin to put on a suitable liniment to this, in a soft cloth over the place of the fracture of that member. Then begin to bandage the member with three or four folds, according to what is fitting for the member: and tighten your hand a little with the bandage.
Then go up with it to the upper part of the place of the fracture, and tighten less than was your stretch, which you bound at the place of the fracture. Then stretch you with the bandage a little, and soften the tight one gradually, until you catch from the healthy place a great thing.
Then take another one carefully, and bandage it again over the place of the fracture with folds. Then go down with the bandage after the fold. And may your operation be in the bandaging and softening of the fold, according to what I said in the first bandaging above.
Then place between the incisions made from the plaster or cloth, as is used for the same degree of twisting in the fracture, if there is a twist in it; and if not, do not put anything into it.
Then place another incision on the same spot. Afterwards, place needles at the same spots immediately, if there is no inflammation and no hot applications.
If however there is inflammation or heat: then place above it the thing that is lying on the heat, and it will remove the inflammation: and let it be for a few days. Then tie up the needles above it.
And let the needles be made from the middle of a cane, sawn in two, and cut into a fine point: or they may be made from wood, from which broom is made, or from palm branches, or from calamus: and the width of all the needles should be according to this form and shape.
However, it should be the needle that is placed on the same piece of flesh that is the largest and most slender, than the others; and the length of the needle should be according to what can be allowed for the member, according to its size and thickness.
Then tie up the needles above the other incision, according to the first tightening. Then tie up below with threads according to the first tightening, as we have said about the binding; and it should be that your binding is higher on the spot of the fracture than the previous one, and the more it extends from the fracture, the smaller the binding.
And it should be that the middle thread is of medium thickness and soft linen.
For if the threads are thick, as is seen in the operation of the stupid ones, their threads from twisted linen fall away because of it: for the binding falls off because of it.
The fine threads do not come together again: for you do not achieve that which you wish through the stricture with them.
It is not necessary for it to be between a star and a star smaller than a finger.

When however there is a fracture with the elbow, and it happens to be disrupted in the skin, I recall it according to its individuality in the chapter.

Common method of ointment, restoring the fracture, suitable for more complexions, especially women and children: for it is from that which does not kindle heat, nor cold.

A method of plastering that is used for the wound and pain. Recipe of mug and chickpeas, and the sharp teeth of human hair, or the feather, and old plants, and all parts in equal amounts: they will be made for, and sheared, and bound, and a plaster will be made from it.

If you see that the pinch, and redness, and pain, and inflammation, and all other things removed completely, and you need plaster and bandage, then repeat this as you did at first equally.
If something of what I said does not happen to the limb, then do not loosen it unless after three days, or four, or five, or seven. And when it has been for twenty days, the whole of this, according to what appears to you from the loosening of the limb, as I said, until the fracture adheres, and the coagulation of the flesh is applied over it: and also at that time in the bandage more than in your first bandage entirely: and also in the increase of weak food, according to what precedes the remembrance of this.
If you see a place where the wound has already dried out and been scraped, and has been rubbed beyond what is necessary: then you know that nourishment is forbidden to be applied to it. Therefore, let the wound be embrocated with warm water at all times where it is possible to apply it, and let it be done for three days, and let it be tightly closed.
Therefore, food is given to the member for this operation, and it heals quickly.
However, what they do with stupid restorers is to give nourishment to the member from the fracture of the limb, when it does not heal at first, according to what is appropriate, and heals according to the tortuosity, it is an error in their operation, and a great fear: and if it were right, they would have said that in their books, and they had operated with it.
And I do not see any of their traces in that at all, and it is better that it is not done.
Regarding the accident that occurred in the head.
The species of the fracture are diverse, and the figures of it are many: and the causes of it are distinct.
For from the fracture is that which happens by a blow with a hammer: and the blow removes the whole bone until it has been moistened to the siphon, which is under the bone, as does the axle in the wood, therefore this species of fracture is called the Axial one.
Sometimes the hammer strikes some bones, and it strikes the face of it, and does not penetrate the cut to the end of it, and this species of fracture is called the Kalan one, that is, Absolute Luxation.
And it is a joint of two fractures, or great or small.
And from the fracture that is abrasion or abrasion, and its cause is a strike with a stone, or a chance on the stone, or such like.
And this fracture is also or perforating, which is approaching the pannicle, which is under the bone: or it is in the face of the bones: and it is a fracture of these two small or large fragments.
And from the fracture that is hidden in the bone in the subtlety of the hair: and it is a small fissure, and for this reason this species of the fracture is called Capillaris.
And from these is a fracture that is made by chance or by a strike with a stone, and such like, which make it go into the slice of the bone to the interior, and it becomes a concussion: just as happens when hot air is struck by them, and it goes into parts of them to the interior.
And this is done most of all in the heads of moist bones, such as are the heads of children.
And all these kinds of fractures are separated and become distinct, and I return to this memory of the whole in its place.
And we know all these kinds of fractures by detection on it, and by the investigation of them when we touch them, and by the removal of the corrupt flesh which is on them.
However, the species of Capillaris is known by this, that it is detected on the bone, and removed, and covered over with wax on it: for the fracture appears black.
However, in the treatment of the fracture, consider first the accidents of the weak: then if you see from the accidents that signify a manifest danger with fear, such as diarrhea, and extension, and loss of intelligence, and glottis, and abscess, and acute fever, and exit of eyes, and redness of them, and such like from many accidents, it is not likely to be cured: and if you see accidents that do not frighten you and hope for health, then begin the care of it.
When it comes to a wound that has first been inflicted, it is necessary to study the removal of bones before the fourthteen day of the month, according to all arrangements.
And if it is in the months of summer, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the flesh under the bone becomes rotten, and those things that we have mentioned will occur.
If the fracture of the bone has already reached the membrane touching the brain, and it is with small pieces, and with attraction, then it is necessary to remove the part that is comminuted and attrited, according to what I will tell you.
And it is like the removal of the head of a wounded head: remove the skull above the bone according to whatever possible way is for you: and according to the shape of the wound, and what is weakest above the weakest.
If it happens to you during the detection of the bone, the flow of blood or hot apostema, then place it with what is necessary next to it. And it is like filling the place with injected membranes in the wine, and rose oil: and make the elbow rest, until the apostema is settled, and be careful about the flow of blood. Then begin in the care of the bone, and its removal.
And it is done according to one of two modes.
One mode is to remove the bone with a scalpel in a straight line: and this is its shape.
Then administer another scalpel after the first one is wide: and this is its shape.
Then also administer another scalpel that is wider than the previous one.
And the second mode is to have a number of scalpels of different sizes: some of which are wider than others, and some of which are narrower than others: and they should be at the end of the last cutting edge, and they should be made of iron or steel: and use ease in percussion on the scalpel, so that it does not hurt the head, and harms it.
If however the bone is strong and hard: then it is necessary to make an incision around its circumference, before you administer the forceps, as the terebras, which are called terebins, do not pierce but cut, and are not called so because they do not reach the end of the cartilage to that which is after it, because the terebra is the rounded extremity above that which is the sharp edge under the head of the bone, similar to a margin, and a smaller ring prevents it from being submerged and passing through the density of the bones.
And it suits you, that you take from these terebras a great number, of which one concurs with the quantity of density of the bones, until the present head of the terebra is before you: whose sharp end in length and breadth is according to the quantity of density of that cranium.
And this is the form of the three kinds of terebras, or trephines.
However, the quality of perforating around the fractured bone is: that you place the terebra on the bone and turn it with your fingers, until you know that the bone has been almost perforated. Then change the terebra to another place, and place that which is between all the holes of the radius in quantity of breadth, or about this.
Then cut with the forceps that is between all the holes of the bone: and make it finer than you can on the end of the fractured part, as we said, until you remove the bone with your hand, or with any other instrument which you have prepared for this, such as tenails, and thin forceps.
And it is necessary that you take all precaution to see that the terebra does not touch the forceps, or any part of the syringe.
When you have surrounded the bone with the drill and separated it from the siphon, if it is continuous with it, and take it out, it is necessary that you sharpen the edges, and make them equal at both ends which remains in the bone with another similar instrument such as an incisor. Nevertheless, it is necessary that it be thinner and more delicate with others of the same type.
If something remains in the bones, and it is hard: then take it with ease, with that which is at your disposal from the instruments. Then take care of the wound after that with the ointments that I have mentioned, and the liniments.
And another method of operation is easy, indeed far from fear: which Galen said and highly praised it, and this is his speech. Then strike it with the hammer from the one side with a small mallet, until you detach the whole bone with ease, as it turns: and you will be secure from the blanket, which does not happen in that which you fear infinitely.
And if the physician were not more foolish than man, and more ignorant of it, and was not sleeping, then if something remained attached to the bone from the blanket in some places, it would detach it from the extremity of the lenticular Incisor of its own, and free it from it with ease. This book is released by him without harm and without fear.

And there is a thing which is not hidden over everything, which in this art is the desire of everyone, and it stands over what we have written and shown in great fractures.

The restoration of the nose when it is broken.
You know that the nose is not broken except when two of its upper parts are broken at the same time, or one of them: for they are two bones: therefore, because they are two bones, it does not break the lower part, which is cartilage, and it does not happen to it except abrasion, tortuosity, and similarity.
If one of its upper parts is broken, then it is necessary to insert a small digit into the nostril, and indicate the fracture with your thumb, and with a deformed finger, until the nose returns to its natural figure: and it should be done artfully, with ease. And beware that it does not happen by your operation on the weak pain.
If the fracture is in the upper part of the nose and does not go to that digit: then it is necessary to make equal to the end of the radius, in which there is a small thickness.
If the fracture is in two parts, then make it like that: and as soon as the restoration is made on the first day of the fracture, if it is possible. And if not, then after the seventh or tenth day, at quiet at night, apply hot sticks.
Then insert into the end of the nose a linen bandage, if the fracture is in one part: or insert two linen bands if the fracture is in two parts: and let the thickness of the linen be so much as to fill the nostril.
And some ancient restorers have said that the linen should be wetted with butter and changed every day. This does not seem to me, but rather it is necessary that the linen be wetted with honey and completely mixed with flour. Then release the linen, until the bone is firm and the cartilage is hardened.
And when it is introduced into the nose at the place of a goose feather, after being covered with soft linen: and it becomes, that it holds the fracture of the nose more firmly, and prevents weakness from inhaling.
And this is not necessary. If you wish, do this: and if you wish, make the linen.
If the nose is burned again while you are working, apply a plaster to the nose with hot oil, or with oil soaked in rose-colored oil, or a small amount of ointment made from alum.
If the nose is not burned hot, then it is necessary to apply a plaster with flour and powdered turmeric with white gum. Then place over the plaster a soft linen bandage, and do not bind the nose tightly with anything.
If the bones of the nose are broken or crushed, then it is necessary to cut under them and take them out with the tools that are suitable for them. Then care for the cut with what becomes inflamed and condensed, and make it strong with suitable plasters or ointments.
If the nostril is injured, then it is necessary to treat it with linen and give a lead tube until it recovers.

¶ About the restoration of the fracture of the spatula.
The spatula is rarely broken, and in the side of its handle: and they are not broken from it except the edges of it.
When therefore it is broken from that place, and it is broken in the middle of its handle, and it is not known except by touch: then according to the figure of the fracture, make a preparation for it. And reduce it over the natural figure of all ways of the genius, which is possible to you.

Then, when the thread is sufficiently long, it should be tied with a firm knot, and held in place with a steady star, until it is no longer removed from its position.
And consider the bandage throughout the day. Whichever way the bandage is softened, tie it up again, and if the starry point is removed from its place: let it be weak on the sound side.
And the spatula will be restored in nineteen days, or in twenty-five days.
When this number is completed, then untie the bandage: and you will be safe. For this is from the bones which are not feared for their union, nor for their separation.
But if it proceeds from a bone fragment, and punctures the skin: then cut it off above, and remove it. And do what I have said in the fracture of the sternum from heat applications, if something comes out of it.
¶ On the restoration of the fracture of the breast.
The breast sometimes breaks in the middle, and this hardly happens. However, the extremities of it are most broken and cut off by its accidents.
When the middle of it breaks, which leans towards the lower parts, and pain, difficulty in breathing, and coughing, and hacking come on, and perhaps blood comes out, and the fracture of the bone is declared, and not hidden from sense: the restoration of it is to be made, so that the weak one lies on the back of its breast: and place between the spatulas of it.
Then press the shoulders of it, and gather up the ribs from two sides or parts with your hands: and make them as equal as possible in this regard, according to all the way that can be done for it, until the figure of the bones returns, according to what is fitting.
Then place the plaster and ointment on top of it, and then place beneath it a star from a thin sheet of glass or salt, or similar, after you have moistened it in the cloth. Then make the bandage thinner over the fractured bone so it does not come loose: and unravel the bandage according to the roundness of the back, and tighten it appropriately.
Then consider the bandage at all times and as often as it softens, tighten it: and if the necessity of its solution arises from pruritus, or corrosion that occurs in the location, or pain, or abscess, then immediately dissolve it, and remove the ointment, and rectify what happens with the mode of its treatment.
Then reduce the ointment, if you see towards that face: and attach it to the tight one, until it heals.

The restoration of a spinal column fracture involves reducing the fracture fragments, aligning the vertebrae, and immobilizing the spine with a brace or cast. The goal is to reestablish the normal anatomy and prevent further displacement of the bones.
While fractures of the collarbone can sometimes occur, they are rare and usually result in a simple fracture. Similarly, fractures of the spinal column are less common but can be more complex to treat. When a fracture occurs in someone, and you want to know if it will heal or not, then trust in the process of healing. If you see the hands of someone who are already softened, stupefied, and lifeless, and cannot move them, extend them, or contract them, and when you contract them with your fingers and press them with a needle, they do not feel any pain, and do not feel any suffering in them, then you know that it is not healing, and there are many ways in which it can be fatal.
If it moves them and they feel a contraction with their fingers and a prick with a needle, then you know that the spine bones are healthy, and that the person will heal with proper treatment.
If you see the spinal bones similar to that one, and you want to know if it will heal or not, then consider the feet of that person. If you see that they are softened, and the same thing happens in their hands, then when they lie on their back, they emit gas and waste without will: and when they are laid on their stomach, they emit gas without will: and when they are laid on their back, and they want to move, and cannot, then you know that it is fatal. ¶ About the restoration of the fracture of the Helper.
This is a spatula, used from the armpit to the head.
If it breaks, then its restoration is according to one of two drachms.
The first is: take a flat wood of medium size, following this shape.
And two cords are tied at the two ends.
Then it is hung from the elevated place: and the weak one sits on the seat. Then he throws his broken arm over the wood, until it reaches the middle of the grain of the wood that is anchored to it.
Then hang something heavy above him, so that it extends his hand to the lower part. Then the physician should examine the broken bones of his hands simultaneously, until the fracture heals according to what is appropriate.
And another method is: let the weak one sit above his neck collar: and hang his hand from the neck of his collar with the cord. Regarding the restoration of the Fracture of the Biceps.
The Biceps is composed of two bones, which are called the two foci.

And it is worse when two bones are broken at once.

If the fractured bone is projecting above the detected skin, then it is necessary to grasp and reduce it yourself, and to make it equal with your hands using ease and gentle extension.

And this is its form.
It is necessary in this operation to place the sharp cut end of it above the projecting end of the bone: and push it with one hand until the bone returns and makes an equal equating.
Therefore, make the extremities of the fracture equal and even.
